BUILDING SEWERS
§ 51.20 BUILDING SEWER PERMITS.
   (A)   No unauthorized person shall uncover, make any connections with or
opening, tap into, use, alter or disturb any public sewer or appurtenance
thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the Building
Commissioner. For all new buildings and connections, the inflow/clearwater
connection to a public sewer shall be made separate and distinct from the
sanitary waste connection. The town shall continuously enforce these
provisions.
   (B)   The owner of a lot, parcel of real estate or building shall make
application, on a special form furnished by the Town Building Inspector, to
construct a building sewer from the building to the main sewer. The permit
application shall be supplemented by any plans, specifications or other
information considered pertinent in the judgment of the Town Building Inspector
and/or Wastewater Department. A permit and inspection fee shall be paid to the
Town Clerk/Treasurer. These permits expire 90 days after the date of their
issuance. The Wastewater Technician may issue a second 90-day permit without
additional charge if application is made prior to the expiration of the first
permit and the application adequately explains why the construction of the
building sewer was not made within the first 90-day period.
   (C)   The owner of a lot, parcel of real estate or building shall make
application on a form supplied by the Wastewater Technician to connect the
building sewer to the public main sewer and to discharge sewage into the public
sewer system. The permit application shall be supplemented by all plans,
specifications or other information from time to time required by the Town
Council. A sewer connection permit and availability fee shall be paid to the
Wastewater Department of the town at the time the application is filed. All
permits issued under this section shall be posted in a prominent place at the
building or construction site.
   (D)   Upon inspection and approval of the connection of a building sewer to
the public main sewer, the owner shall become a customer of the POTW and shall
be subject to all applicable policies, rules, rates and charges.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.21 COST OF INSTILLATION.
   All costs and expenses incidental to the installation and connection of the
building sewer shall be paid by the owner. The owner or the person installing
the building sewer for the owner shall indemnify the town for any loss or
damage that may be directly or indirectly occasioned by the installation.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020)
§ 51.22 INDEPENDENT SEWER REQUIRED.
   (A)   A separate and independent building sewer shall be provided for every
building, except where one building is located at the rear of another and no
private sewer is available or can be constructed to the rear building through
an adjoining alley, courtyard or driveway, and the owner(s) obtain approval for
extension and connection, and the sewer serving the front building is
determined by the Wastewater Technician to be adequate to handle both
facilities.
   (B)   Other exceptions will be allowed only by special permission granted by
the Wastewater Department.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020)
§ 51.23 INSPECTION OF EXISTING BUILDING SEWERS BEFORE USE.
   Existing building sewers may be used in connection with new buildings only
when they are found, by inspection and testing by the Wastewater Technician, to
meet all requirements of this chapter.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020)
§ 51.24 CONFORMANCE WITH CODES REQUIRED.
   The size, slope, alignment and materials of construction of a building
sewer, and the methods to be used in excavating, placing the pipe, jointing,
testing and backfilling the trench, shall all conform to the requirements of
the building and plumbing codes or other applicable rules, regulations and
construction standards of the town and this state.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.25 GRAVITY FLOW.
   Whenever possible, the building sewer shall be brought to the building at an
elevation below the basement floor. When the building drain is too low to
permit gravity flow to the public sewer, sanitary wastewater carried by the
building drain shall be lifted by a means approved by the town and discharged
to the building sewer.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020)
§ 51.26 CONNECTING RUNOFF OR GROUNDWATER WITH SANITARY SEWER PROHIBITED.
   No person shall make a connection of roof down spouts, exterior foundation
drains, areaway drains or other sources of surface runoff, groundwater or
uncontaminated cooling water to a building sewer or building drain, including
any stormwater sump pumps. Persons who connect such facilities to the sewer
system shall be responsible for properly disconnecting the same upon
notification of the town. Persons in violation of this chapter shall be subject
to penalties as defined herein. Stormwater and all other unpolluted drainage
shall be discharged to sewers specifically designated as storm sewers, or to a
natural outlet approved by the town.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.27 INSPECTION FOR BUILDING SEWERS REQUIRED.
   The applicant for the building sewer permit shall notify the Wastewater
Technician when the building sewer is ready for inspection. The connection
shall be made under the supervision of the Inspector or his or her
representative. Building sewer permit applicants shall notify the Wastewater
Technician when the building sewer is ready for inspection and connection to
the public sewer. All connections to the public sewer shall be made under the
supervision of the Wastewater Technician or his or her representative. Notice
shall be given at least 48 hours in advance to allow the Inspector to schedule
a time for inspection and connection.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.28 BUILDING SEWER CONNECTION REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   The connection of the building sewer to the public sewer shall conform
to the requirements of the building and plumbing codes or other applicable
rules and regulations of the town. The connection of the building sewer to the
wastewater system shall only be permitted by a contractor authorized by the
town.
   (B)   The applicant for the building sewer permit shall notify the
Wastewater Technician when the building sewer is ready for inspection and
connection to the public sewer. The connection shall be made under the
supervision of the Wastewater Technician or his or her representative. Notice
shall be given at least 48 hours in advance to allow the Wastewater Technician
to schedule a time for the inspection. It shall be a violation of this chapter
for any connection to be covered prior to final inspection and approval by the
Town Building Inspector. If re-excavation is required to permit inspection, the
property owner shall be responsible and shall reimburse the town for all
expenses incurred. The owner shall be responsible for obtaining and complying
with street cut permits from the appropriate agencies as well as any other
permits, authorizations and/or utility service locations required to facilitate
a building sewer connection.
   (C)   All excavations for building sewer installations shall be adequately
guarded by the owner with barricades and lights so as to protect the public
from hazard. Streets, alleys, sidewalks, parkways and other public property
disturbed in the course of work shall be restored to a safe condition in a
manner satisfactory to the Town Building Inspector.
   (D)   The owner shall agree to indemnify and hold harmless the town from any
loss, damage, claims or actions that may directly or indirectly be occasioned
by installation of the building sewer.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020) Penalty, see §
51.99
DISCHARGE AND TREATMENT REQUIREMENTS
§ 51.40 PROHIBITED AND RESTRICTED DISCHARGES.
   (A)   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged into a public
sewer any of the following:
      (1)   Gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil or other flammable or
explosive liquids, solids or gases;
      (2)   Any waters or wastes containing toxic or poisonous solids, liquids
or gases in sufficient quantity, either singularly or by interaction with other
wastes, to injure or interfere with any sewage treatment process, constitute a
hazard to humans or animals, create a public nuisance or create any hazard in
the receiving waters of the POTW;
      (3)   Any waters or wastes having properties capable of damaging or
causing hazards to the structures, equipment and/or personnel of the Wastewater
Department; or
      (4)   Solid or viscous substances in quantities or of a size capable of
causing flow obstructions in the sewers or other interference with the proper
operation of the POTW.
   (B)   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged the described
substances, materials, waters or wastes if it appears likely, in the opinion of
the Wastewater Technician, that such wastes can harm either the sewers,
wastewater treatment process or equipment, or have an adverse effect on the
receiving stream, or otherwise endanger life, limb or public property, or
constitute a nuisance. In making his or her decision as to the acceptability of
these wastes, the Wastewater Technician will give consideration to such factors
as the quantities of subject wastes in relation to the flows and velocities in
the sewers, materials of construction of the sewers, nature of the wastewater
treatment process, capacity of the wastewater treatment plant, degree of
treatability of wastes in the wastewater treatment plant and pertinent factors.
   (C)   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged water or wastes
containing substances which are not amendable to treatment or reduction by the
wastewater treatment processes employed, or are amendable to treatment only to
such a degree that the wastewater treatment plant effluent cannot meet the
requirements of other agencies having jurisdiction over discharge to the
receiving waters.
   (D)   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged into a public
sewer any of the following: stormwater, surface water, groundwater, roof
runoff, subsurface drainage, non-contract cooling water, swimming pool water or
other unpolluted water. Stormwater and all other unpolluted drainage shall be
discharged to designated stormwater sewers.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.41 DISCHARGE RULES AND RESTRICTIONS APPLY.
   All system users are subject to the discharging rules and restrictions
expressly set forth in this chapter and all applicable EPA National
Pretreatment Standards, and state and local standards, all of which are
incorporated herein by reference.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020)
§ 51.42 DISCHARGE OF PROHIBITED OR RESTRICTED SUBSTANCES.
   (A)   If any waters or wastes are discharged, or are proposed to be
discharged, to the public sewers which contain prohibited substances or
characteristics which, in the judgment of the Wastewater Technician or his or
her representatives, may have a deleterious effect on the POTW or receiving
waters, or which otherwise create a hazard to life or constitute a public
nuisance, the Wastewater Technician may:
      (1)   Reject the wastes;
      (2)   Require pretreatment to an acceptable condition for discharge to
the public sewers;
      (3)   Require control over the quantities and rates of discharge; or
      (4)   Require payment to cover the added cost of handling and treating
the wastes not covered by existing taxes or sewer charges under the provisions
of §
51.04 of this chapter.
   (B)   If the Wastewater Technician permits the pretreatment or equalization
of waste flow, the design and installation of the plants and equipment shall be
subject to the requirements of all applicable federal, state and local
statutes, rules, regulations and ordinances.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.43 GREASE, OIL AND SAND INTERCEPTORS.
   (A)   Grease, soap, oil and sand interceptors shall be provided when, in the
opinion of the Wastewater Technician, they are necessary for the proper
handling of liquid wastes containing grease in excessive amounts, or any
flammable wastes, sand, soap or other harmful ingredients.
   (B)   All interceptors shall be of a type and capacity approved by the
Wastewater Technician and shall be located as to be readily and easily
accessible for cleaning and inspection.
   (C)   Costs incurred by the town to correct problems in or repair damage to
the POTW caused by a violation of these provisions shall be reimbursed by the
owner of the property which is the source of the discharge
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.44 PRELIMINARY TREATMENT FACILITIES.
   Where preliminary treatment of flow-equalizing facilities are provided for
any waters or wastes, they shall be maintained continuously in a manner
approved by the Wastewater Technician at the owner’s sole expense.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020)
§ 51.45 TESTS, MEASUREMENTS AND ANALYSES.
   (A)   Measurement. All measurements, tests and analyses of the
characteristics of waters and wastes to which reference is made in this chapter
shall be determined in accordance with the latest edition of “Standard Methods
for the Examination of Water and Wastewater.”
   (B)   Sampling and analysis. Sampling shall be carried out by customarily
accepted methods to reflect the effect of constituents on the sewage works and
to determine the existence of hazards to life, limb and property.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020)
ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
§ 51.60 OBJECTIONABLE MATERIAL PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to place or deposit, or permit to be
placed or deposited, in any unsanitary manner on public or private property
within the town, or in any area under the jurisdiction of the town, any sewage
or other polluted waters. It shall be unlawful to discharge to any natural
outlet or watercourse within the town, or in any area under the jurisdiction of
the town, any sewage or other polluted waters. It shall be unlawful to
construct or maintain any facility intended or used for the disposal of
wastewater except as provided in §
51.03 of this chapter.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.61 PROTECTION FROM DAMAGE.
   No unauthorized person shall maliciously, willfully or negligently break,
damage, destroy, uncover, deface or tamper with any structure, appurtenance or
equipment which is a part of the municipal sewage works. Any person violating
this provision shall be subject to immediate arrest under charge of disorderly
conduct.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020) Penalty, see §
51.99
§ 51.62 POWERS AND AUTHORITY OF INSPECTORS.
   The Wastewater Department, Inspector and other duly authorized employees of
the town bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to
enter upon all properties for the purpose of inspection, observation,
measurement, sampling and testing, in accordance with the provisions of this
chapter.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020)
§ 51.63 REMEDIES FOR VIOLATIONS.
   (A)   Any person found to be in violation of the provisions of this chapter
or who discharges or causes to be discharged any material causing damage to or
obstructing the POTW will be liable to the town for any expense, losses or
damages caused by the violation or discharge. The town may recover all
expenses, losses, damages or fines by any or all equitable or legal remedies.
This remedy shall be in addition to all others provided by law or this chapter.
   (B)   In addition to all other remedies, the town may bring a civil action
to enforce the provisions of this chapter in accordance with I.C. 36-1-6.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020)
§ 51.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is provided shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   Any person who violates an order of the town or fails to comply
strictly with this chapter shall be subject to the imposition of a civil
penalty of up to $2,500, in addition to all other remedies created which may be
available at law and in equity. Each day’s violation shall constitute a
separate offense for which a separate fine may be imposed.
(Ord. 2020-1, passed 1-29-2020; Ord. 2020-13, passed 6-8-2020)
CHAPTER 52: WATER
Section
   
52.01   Payment of fire hydrant rental costs
§ 52.01 PAYMENT OF FIRE HYDRANT RENTAL COSTS.
   (A)   The provisions of I.C. 8-1-2-103(d) are hereby adopted such that the
charges for production, storage, transmission, sale and delivery or furnishing
of water for public fire protection purposes shall be added to the basic rates
of all customers of Indiana American Water Company and its successors and
assigns as regulated by the State Utility Regulatory Commission.
   (B)   The effective date for the addition of these changes in the basic rate
shall be November 1, 2019, and after said date, the cost of any fire hydrant
installed at the request of the town shall be paid by or on behalf of the town.
(Ord. 2019-11, passed - -2019)
CHAPTER 53: STORMWATER
Section
Stormwater User Fee
   
53.01   Fee imposed; effective date
   
53.02   Payment; late or insufficient payments
   
53.03   Fee amount
STORMWATER USER FEE
§ 53.01 FEE IMPOSED; EFFECTIVE DATE.
   (A)   A stormwater user fee shall be imposed on each and every lot and
parcel of land within the town which directly or indirectly contributes to the
stormwater system of the town, which charge shall be assessed against the
owner. Each property or parcel assigned a separate tax identification number
shall be individually subject to the stormwater user fee. This charge is deemed
reasonable and is the minimum necessary to pay for the repair, replacement,
planning, improvement, operation, regulation and maintenance of the existing
and future town stormwater system.
   (B)   The stormwater user fee shall be in effect the date of the ordinance
codified in this section, and shall be due and payable on or before the dates
shown on the billing statement.
(Ord. 2018-1, passed 1-23-2018)
§ 53.02 PAYMENT; LATE OR INSUFFICIENT PAYMENTS.
   (A)   (1)   The stormwater user fee shall be due on the payment date set out
in the billing statement. It shall be a violation of this subchapter to fail to
pay a stormwater billing statement when due. All bills for stormwater services
not paid on or before the due date shall be subject to a collection or deferred
payment charge of 10% on the outstanding balance. Payments
returned for non-sufficient funds shall be subject to an additional fee of $20.
      (2)   Partial payments shall be applied in this order:
         (a)   Any non-sufficient funds fees on the account;
         (b)   Any late fees on the account;
         (c)   Past-due balances; and
         (d)   Current balances.
   (B)   Delinquent stormwater service charges and applied penalties, recording
fees and service charges may be made a lien upon property and may be collected
in accordance with state law.
(Ord. 2018-1, passed 1-23-2018)
§ 53.03 FEE AMOUNT.
   The stormwater user fee shall be a monthly user fee of $5.
(Ord. 2018-1, passed 1-23-2018)

§ 70.01 ACCIDENT REPORTS; FEES.
   (A)   There is hereby set a fee of $5 for each accident report provided as
requested.
   (B)   The fee shall be deposited in a separate account, to be known as the
“Accident Report Account.”
   (C)   The funds may be expended only at the discretion of the chief officer
of the Police Department, or for any department purpose reasonably related to
the keeping of accident reports and records of the prevention of street and
highway accidents.
(Prior Code, § 70.01) (Ord. 406, passed 9-6-1988)
§ 70.02 REGULATIONS GOVERNING SPECIFIC STREETS ADOPTED.
   The Town Council, acting within the reasonable exercise of its police power,
hereby adopts the regulations governing certain roads and streets under its
jurisdiction as set out in the traffic schedules in Chapter 75 of this code.
(Prior Code, § 70.02) Penalty, see §
70.99

is otherwise provided shall be fined an amount not to exceed $2,500.
(Prior Code, § 70.99) (Ord. 358, passed 1-8-1974)
CHAPTER 71: TRAFFIC REGULATIONS
Section
   
71.01   Driving on sidewalks prohibited
   
71.02   Exceeding posted speed limit prohibited
   
71.03   Disregarding stop sign prohibited
   
71.04   Disregarding law enforcement officer prohibited
   
71.05   Disregarding railroad signal prohibited
§ 71.01 DRIVING ON SIDEWALKS PROHIBITED.
   No persons shall drive a motor vehicle on any sidewalk.
(Prior Code, § 71.02) (Ord. 358, passed 1-8-1974; Ord. 507, passed 4-20-2005)
Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.02 EXCEEDING POSTED SPEED LIMIT PROHIBITED.
   No person shall drive a motor vehicle on any street, or portion thereof,
within the jurisdiction of the town at a speed in excess of that which is
posted by sign to be the maximum safe speed for that street or portion thereof.
(Prior Code, § 71.03) (Ord. 507, passed 4-20-2005) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.03 DISREGARDING STOP SIGN PROHIBITED.
   No person shall drive a motor vehicle on any street, or portion thereof,
within the jurisdiction of the town and fail to come to a complete stop at any
intersection where a stop sign has been posted.
(Prior Code, § 71.04) (Ord. 507, passed 4-20-2005) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.04 DISREGARDING LAW ENFORCEMENT OFFICER PROHIBITED.
   No person shall drive a motor vehicle on any street, or portion thereof,
within the jurisdiction of the town and fail to comply with the lawful order or
direction of a law enforcement officer vested by law with the authority to
direct, control or regulate the movement of traffic.
(Prior Code, § 71.05) (Ord. 507, passed 4-20-2005) Penalty, see §
70.99
§ 71.05 DISREGARDING RAILROAD SIGNAL PROHIBITED.
   No person shall drive a motor vehicle on any street, or portion thereof,
within the jurisdiction of the town and fail to stop at a railroad crossing
when:
   (A)   A clearly visible electric or mechanical signal device gives warning
of the immediate approach of a train;
   (B)   A crossing gate is lowered, or when a human flagger gives signal to
stop for the approach of a train;
   (C)   A railroad train is approaching within 1,500 feet of a street crossing
and emits an audible signal of its approach; or
   (D)   The railroad train is clearly visible and is in hazardous proximity to
the crossing.
(Prior Code, § 71.06) (Ord. 507, passed 4-20-2005) Penalty, see §
70.99
CHAPTER 72: PARKING REGULATIONS
Section
   
72.01   Limitations on parking and standing
   
72.02   Authority to restrict parking
   
72.03   Authority to remove vehicle
   
72.04   Exception for authorized emergency vehicles
   
72.05   Violations; discount for timely payment
   
72.06   Parking of trucks and buses
 
   
72.99   Penalty
§ 72.01 LIMITATIONS ON PARKING AND STANDING.
   (A)   No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle, except when necessary
to avoid conflict with other traffic or to avoid conflict with law or the
directions of a police officer or traffic-control device, in any of the places
set forth in this chapter, or
Chapter 76, Schedule I, of this code, where signs have been erected by the Town
Council prohibiting parking.
   (B)   No person shall stop, park or leave standing any motor vehicle,
whether attended or unattended, upon the paved or main traveled portion of any
highway within the town.
   (C)   No person shall park within 15 feet of a fire hydrant.
   (D)   No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle, except when necessary
to avoid conflict with other traffic-control devices, in any of the following
places:
      (1)   On a sidewalk;
      (2)   In front of a public or private driveway;
      (3)   On a crosswalk; or
      (4)   On an alleyway.
(Prior Code, § 72.01) (Ord. 358, passed 1-8-1974) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.02 AUTHORITY TO RESTRICT PARKING.
   The Town Marshal, Deputy Marshals or the Street Commissioner are authorized
and empowered on an emergency basis, and by posting of written notice, to
restrict parking on any street in the town for a period not to exceed 30
continuous days. The written notice shall be posted in the area where the
parking is to be restricted in a manner where it shall be clearly visible to
all motorists.
(Prior Code, § 72.02) (Ord. 358, passed 1-8-1974)
§ 72.03 AUTHORITY TO REMOVE VEHICLE.
   The Town Marshal or Deputy Marshals are authorized to move motor vehicles
parked in violation of this chapter, or
Chapter 76, Schedule I, of this code, or to require the driver or other persons
in charge of any motor vehicle violating any provision of this chapter to move
the vehicle. If the vehicle is unattended, then the officer is authorized to
provide for the removal of the vehicle to the nearest available garage or other
place of safety.
(Prior Code, § 72.03) (Ord. 358, passed 1-8-1974)
§ 72.04 EXCEPTION FOR AUTHORIZED EMERGENCY VEHICLES.
   The stopping, standing and parking limitations set forth in this chapter, or
Chapter 76, Schedule I, of this code, shall not apply to authorized emergency
vehicles.
(Prior Code, § 72.04) (Ord. 358, passed 1-8-1974)
§ 72.05 VIOLATIONS; DISCOUNT FOR TIMELY PAYMENT.
   Any person violating the provisions of this chapter, or
Chapter 76, Schedule I, of this code, shall be subject to the penalty provided
in §
72.99. Any person violating the provisions of this chapter, or
Chapter 76, Schedule I, of this code, for the first time may, within five days
of receiving the citation, plead guilty and be fined a sum of $10, to be paid
to the Clerk/Treasurer.
(Prior Code, § 72.05) (Ord. 358, passed 1-8-1974) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.06 PARKING OF TRUCKS AND BUSES.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      BUSINESS DISTRICT. Beginning at the intersection of Church Street and
Main Street and continuing northward on Main Street to the northern limit of
Main Street at the town’s boundary.
      RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT. The remainder of the town shall be considered
within the RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT.
      VEHICLES. Trucks, trailers, recreational vehicles, buses, tractors or
tractor-trailers which are wider, longer or taller than a conventional station
wagon or pickup truck.
   (B)   Residential District. No person owning or operating a truck, trailer,
bus, recreational vehicle, tractor or tractor and trailer which is wider,
longer or taller than a conventional station wagon or pickup truck shall park
that vehicle on or upon any street or alley within any residential district.
This division (B) shall not prevent any vehicle from parking for a sufficient
time to make deliveries or pick up merchandise if the parking does not
interrupt the regular traffic flow and does not create a safety hazard.
   (C)   Business District. No person shall park any vehicle, as defined in
division (A) above, upon any street or alley longer than one hour within any
business district. This division (C) shall not prevent any vehicle from parking
for a sufficient time to make deliveries or pick up merchandise in the regular
course of business if the parking does not interrupt regular traffic flow and
does not create a safety hazard.
   (D)   Police Department permission. Any vehicle, as defined herein, may park
on or upon any street or alley in a business or residential district if the
owner of the vehicle has first obtained written permission from the Police
Department. The permit shall state the location where the vehicle may be parked
and the duration for which the parking shall be allowed.
(Prior Code, § 72.06) (Ord. 431, passed 7-11-1995) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is provided shall be subject to §
70.99 of this code.
   (B)   Any person who violates any provision of §
72.06 of this chapter and is found guilty of said violation shall be fined not
more than $100 for each violation. If any person is convicted of a third or
subsequent offense committed within one year after the date of the first
offense, that person shall be fined not more than $1,000. Each day a violation
continues constitutes a separate offense.
(Prior Code, § 72.06) (Ord. 431, passed 7-11-1995)
CHAPTER 73: GOLF CARTS AND RECREATIONAL OFF-ROAD VEHICLES
Section
   
73.01   Definitions
   
73.02   Operation restrictions
   
73.03   Operator requirements
   
73.04   Financial responsibility
   
73.05   Occupant restrictions
   
73.06   Traffic rule obeyance
   
73.07   Places of operation and storage
   
73.08   Street use permit registration and issuance; fee
   
73.09   Enforcement
   
73.99   Penalty
Cross-reference:
   Motorized vehicles not required to be plated, see
Chapter 74
§ 73.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   DRIVER’S LICENSE. A valid license to operate a motor vehicle issued by this
state or any state.
   FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY. Liability insurance coverage on a golf cart or
recreational off-road vehicle in an amount not less than required by state law
for motor vehicles operated on public highways in the state.
   GOLF CART. A vehicle with four wheels originally designed for operation on a
golf course and powered by a battery or internal combustion motor, and has a
factory-manufactured set of working head lights, taillights and brake lights.
   RECREATIONAL OFF-ROAD VEHICLE. A motorized off-highway vehicle that:
      (1)   Is 72 inches or less in width;
      (2)   Is designed for travel on a maximum of four non-highway or off-
highway tires;
      (3)   Is designed for recreations use by one or more individuals;
      (4)   Has a non-straddle seat or saddle;
      (5)   Has a steering wheel for steering control;
      (6)   Is not a lawn mower or a motorized bicycle; and
      (7)   Has a factory-manufactured set of working head lights, taillights
and brake lights.
(Ord. 2023-8, passed 12-6-2023)
§ 73.02 OPERATION RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   The operation of recreational off-road vehicles is strictly prohibited
and not permitted anywhere on public property within the town.
   (B)   The operation of a golf cart within the town is strictly prohibited
unless the golf cart is operated and equipped in full compliance with this
chapter.
   (C)   This chapter does not apply to municipally owned golf carts used for
maintenance, public safety or special events.
(Ord. 2023-8, passed 12-6-2023) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.03 OPERATOR REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   Only valid licensed drivers 16 years of age or older, and issued a
driver’s license from a state’s bureau of motor vehicles, may operate a golf
cart on streets, alleys and public property under the jurisdiction of the town.
   (B)   The owner of a golf cart may not cause or knowingly permit an
individual to operate the golf cart on streets, alleys and public property
under the jurisdiction of the town unless the individual holds a valid driver’s
license from a state’s bureau of motor vehicles.
(Ord. 2023-8, passed 12-6-2023) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.04 FINANCIAL RESPONSIBILITY.
   (A)   The operator of a golf cart must show financial responsibility when
operating a golf cart on property under the jurisdiction of the town.
   (B)   Written proof of financial responsibility for the operator must be
available on the golf cart.
(Ord. 2023-8, passed 12-6-2023) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.05 OCCUPANT RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   The number of occupants in a golf cart shall be limited to the number
of persons for whom factory seating was installed and provided.
   (B)   The operator and all occupant(s) shall be seated in the golf cart, and
no part of the body of the operator or occupant(s) shall extend outside the
perimeter of the golf cart while the golf cart is being operated on public
property under the jurisdiction of the town.
   (C)   No one under the age of eight is allowed to ride on the back seat of
the golf cart unless accompanied by an adult.
(Ord. 2023-8, passed 12-6-2023) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.06 TRAFFIC RULE OBEYANCE.
   (A)   Golf carts shall obey all the rules of the road for vehicles,
including traffic signs and markings.
   (B)   Golf carts shall display a “slow-moving vehicle” sign of the same type
required under state law.
   (C)   Golf carts shall display a registration permit sticker from the town
valid for the current year.
(Ord. 2023-8, passed 12-6-2023) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.07 PLACES OF OPERATION AND STORAGE.
   (A)   Golf carts in compliance with this chapter may be operated on all
streets and alleys within the corporate limits of the town.
   (B)   Golf carts are prohibited to be operated on any sidewalk, walking
trail, bike path, park path or any other place where the use of vehicles is
prohibited.
   (C)   Golf carts must be stored on private property on an approved parking
surface.
   (D)   Golf carts must follow the parking rules adopted by the town for all
other motor vehicles.
(Ord. 2023-8, passed 12-6-2023) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.08 STREET USE PERMIT REGISTRATION AND ISSUANCE; FEE.
   (A)   No golf cart may operate within the town corporate limits without
first registering and obtaining a street use permit.
   (B)   Since the town will incur administrative costs related to the
inspection and printing of the permit decal, the fee for the street use permit
shall be $25 for the initial permit.
   (C)   The renewal fee shall be $25 per year.
   (D)   All permits will expire on March 31 and renewals will be due annually
on April 1.
   (E)   Before a permit may be issued, the owner of the golf cart must fill
out a permit application form, which will be available through the Clerk’s/
Treasurer’s Office or the Town Police Department.
   (F)   The Town Police Department will conduct inspections via appointment
only to ensure that the requisite equipment is in working order.
   (G)   The inspection will only be done to determine if the golf cart
complies with this chapter. It is the responsibility of the owner to keep the
golf cart in good working order and in compliance with ordinance and applicable
state statutes or be subject to all fines and penalties under the law.
   (H)   The inspection will do the following:
      (1)   Verify the VIN number;
      (2)   Determine occupancy based on the number of installed seats;
      (3)   Verify two factory head lights are operational;
      (4)   Verify two factory taillights are operational;
      (5)   Verify two factory brake lights are operation and visible from a
minimum of 500 feet; and
      (6)   Verify proof of financial responsibility.
   (I)   The inspection will not test any mechanical components of the golf
carts, such as brakes. The town is not equipped and is not testing for the
general mechanical quality of the golf cart and accepts no liability for the
maintenance or operation of a golf cart.
   (J)   Once the police inspection has been satisfactorily completed, and upon
payment of the fee, the Clerk’s office shall issue a street use permit.
   (K)   To operate on authorized public property under the jurisdiction of the
town, a golf cart must display the street use permit on the rear of the golf
cart and must display the slow-moving vehicle sign.
(Ord. 2023-8, passed 12-6-2023) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.09 ENFORCEMENT.
   Violation notices issued under this chapter may be issued by a sworn member
of the Town Police Department, the code enforcement officer, any designated
parking enforcement officer or any other duly authorized town inspector or
designated code enforcement agent or assistant.
(Ord. 2023-8, passed 12-6-2023)
§ 73.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is provided shall be subject to §
70.99 of this code.
   (B)   (1)   The civil penalty for the first violation notice issued under
this chapter shall be $50.
      (2)   The civil penalty for the second violation notice issued under this
chapter shall be $100.
      (3)   Subsequent violations may result in the impoundment of the golf
cart and/or revocation of the street use permit.
      (4)   It shall be the responsibility of the duly authorized town officer/
inspector who is issuing the violation notice to determine and designate on the
violation notice if this is a first, second or subsequent offense.
      (5)   The Violations Clerk has the authority to add a late fee of $25 for
any violation which is not paid within 60 days of issuance.
(Ord. 2023-8, passed 12-6-2023)

§ 74.01 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this chapter, ALTERNATIVE TRANSPORTATION is described as
any motorized vehicle not requiring to be plated, including, but not limited
to, utility carts, quad runners, dirt bikes and ATV-style vehicles.
(Ord. 522, passed 8-15-2007; Ord. 2024-4, passed 6-6-2024)
§ 74.02 DRIVER’S LICENSE AND COMPLIANCE REQUIRED.
   Any operator of alternative transportation must have a current and valid
driver’s license and comply with local and state ordinances and laws.
(Ord. 522, passed 8-15-2007; Ord. 522 A, passed 10-6-2009) Penalty, see §
74.99
§ 74.03 ANNUAL INSPECTIONS; INSPECTION STICKER.
   (A)   Any alternative transportation vehicle or device must be inspected on
an annual basis. The inspection cost is $25 per unit, and the inspection shall
be conducted by the Town Police Department. The purpose of the inspection will
be to determine whether or not the unit is safe and in compliance with all
related rules and regulations.
   (B)   Any alternative vehicle that operates on town streets must be
registered and inspected by the Town Police Department. Each unit shall be
issued an inspection sticker. The sticker is to be placed in plain view and on
the driver’s side one inch below the driver’s seat.
(Ord. 522, passed 8-15-2007) Penalty, see §
74.99
§ 74.04 INSPECTION RENEWAL.
   The owner of the alternative vehicle must renew the inspection every 12
months. The Town Police Department shall maintain a record of inspections and
reserves the right to remove any uninspected or unsafe alternative
transportation unit.
(Ord. 522, passed 8-15-2007) Penalty, see §
74.99
§ 74.05 EQUIPMENT REQUIRED.
   Each unit shall have a seat belt for each passenger. Each unit shall have
operating head lights and taillights. All rules and laws apply to alternative
vehicles that apply to regular motor vehicles.
(Ord. 522, passed 8-15-2007) Penalty, see §
74.99
§ 74.06 INSURANCE REQUIRED.
   Each alternative transportation unit shall be insured by the owner, and
proof of insurance shall be provided at the inspection time and be carried on
the alternative vehicle at all times.
(Ord. 522, passed 8-15-2007) Penalty, see §
74.99
§ 74.07 PARKING.
   Parking will be parallel to and on the right in the same direction as the
traffic is designated to flow and in designated parking areas.
(Ord. 522, passed 8-15-2007) Penalty, see §
74.99
§ 74.08 TOWING OF VEHICLE.
   Vehicles may be towed at the officer’s discretion.
(Ord. 522, passed 8-15-2007)
§ 74.99 PENALTY.
   Any violator of this chapter shall be cited into a local court and subject
to fines listed below:
   (A)   No, or un-operating, head lights or taillights: $50;
   (B)   No inspection sticker: $50;
   (C)   No seat belt/seat belt not used: $25 per violation; and
   (D)   Outdated inspection sticker: $25.
(Ord. 522, passed 8-15-2007)

SCHEDULE I. SPEED LIMITS.
   (A)   The Town Council, having determined that the maximum speed permitted
by state statute is greater than what is reasonable and safe under the
conditions found to exist on certain streets, or portions thereof, hereby
declares the following to be the reasonable and safe maximum speed limits on
the streets, or portions thereof, listed in divisions (B), (C) and (D) below.
   (B)   It is hereby determined that the speed permitted by state law on the
following streets, or portions thereof, is greater than is reasonable and safe
under the conditions found to exist upon those streets, or portions thereof.
The Council hereby determines that the maximum speed limit for the streets, or
portions thereof, listed below shall be 20 mph.
Street Location
Street                 Location
Broadway Street        North from Delaware Street to Mill Street
Delaware Street        West from Third Street to the dead end
East North Main Street North from New York Street to town limits

John Street            West from Seventh Street to Summit Street
Mill Street            West from Broadway Street to Summit Street
Seventh Street         North from Lake Street to Mill Street
Summit Street          North from John Street to Mill Street
 
   (C)   It is hereby determined, upon the basis of traffic and engineering
investigations, that the proper maximum speed for all streets, or portions
thereof, and urban districts not governed by the provisions of division (B)
above shall be 30 mph. The Council hereby determines that the maximum speed
limit for these streets, or portions thereof, listed below shall be 30 mph.

SCHEDULE IV. MOTOR VEHICLES WITH THREE OR MORE AXELS.
   (A)   Definition. As used in this schedule, THROUGH-TRAFFIC refers to
traffic initiated at and destined for points outside the town.
   (B)   Prohibitions.
      (1)   Unless a detour route has been posted or a police officer otherwise
directs, through-traffic is hereby prohibited for all motor vehicles with three
or more axles except for on the following town streets: Main Street.
      (2)   All motor vehicles with three or more axles are prohibited from
crossing the railway tracks on the following town streets:
         (a)   Walnut Street; and
         (b)   Mill Street.
(Ord. 2018-3, passed 7-3-2018) Penalty, see §
70.99
SCHEDULE V. HEAVY TRUCK TRAFFIC.
   (A)   Preamble.
      (1)   The town has the authority to regulate the heavy truck traffic
within the limits of the town.
      (2)   Large, heavy vehicles cause extraordinary damage to the
infrastructure of local roadways and are an unhealthy source of noise and
pollution. The operation of the ethanol plant south of the town is expected to
substantially increase the number of large heavy vehicles utilizing town-,
county- and state-maintained roadways in the area. The increasing
infrastructure damage to town- and county-maintained roadways caused by the
increasing regular use of large heavy vehicles includes damage to the roadway
surface, subgrade, sidewalks, curbs and pavement markings because those
facilities were not designed for the predicted volumes of vehicles of that size
and weight. Repair of the damage to the roadway surface, subgrade, sidewalks,
curbs and markings is costly to the town and its citizens and puts an
unnecessary burden on limited town resources by causing these elements of the
roadway to fail much sooner than anticipated.
      (3)   It is not the nature nor purpose of the local street system to
convey traffic that is not destined for a location within the town. It is the
nature and purpose of state- and county-maintained roadways to convey the
volumes, weights and sizes of vehicles destined for and originating from the
ethanol plant and other commercial facilities.
   (B)   Definitions. For the purpose of this schedule, the following terms,
phrases, words and their derivations shall have the meanings given herein.
      HEAVY TRUCK. Any motor vehicle or towed vehicle with a gross vehicle
weight rating (GVWR), registered gross vehicle weight rating (RGVW) or an
actual weight, whichever is greater, of 26,001 pounds or more; or any
combination of vehicles where the gross combined weight rating (GCWR), total
registered gross vehicle weight (RGVW) or the actual weight of the combination
is 26,001 pounds or more.
      SHALL. It is always mandatory and not merely directory.
   (C)   No heavy truck traffic. It shall be unlawful for any person operating
a heavy truck, as defined in division (B) above, to travel on any street in the
town other than First Street.
   (D)   Required use generally; exceptions. This schedule shall not prohibit:
      (1)   The operation of heavy trucks upon any street where necessary to
the conduct of a commercial enterprise (“in commerce”) for the purpose of
making a scheduled or definite stop within the town limits at a destination
point. The operator of such truck shall keep a log book, delivery slip or other
evidence of his or her destination and point of origin;
      (2)   The operation of emergency vehicles upon any street in the town;
      (3)   The operation of heavy trucks owned or operated by the town, public
utilities, any contractor or materialperson while engaged in the repair,
maintenance or construction of streets, street improvements or street utilities
with the town;
      (4)   The operation of heavy trucks upon any officially established
detour in any case where such truck could lawfully be operated upon the street
for which such detour is established; or
      (5)   Use by heavy trucks which originate within the town limits.
However, said heavy trucks shall proceed from their point of origin by the
shortest route possible to a roadway outside the town limits.
(Ord. 534, passed 11-11-2008) Penalty, see §
70.99

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 90.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ANIMAL. Any live, non-human vertebrate creature, domestic or wild.
   AT LARGE. Not under restraint, as defined in this section.
   DOMESTIC ANIMAL. A domestic animal, as defined by state law, but not a dog
used to aid a blind person.
   HARBORING. Permitting any animal to remain or to be fed within any person’s
enclosure, place of business, residence or any premises controlled by that
person for more than three consecutive days.
   OWNER. Any person harboring an animal.
   PERSON. A person, as defined by state law.
   PUBLIC NUISANCE. Any animal which is at large, or which attacks or molests
other animals, humans or passing vehicles, or which damages property, or which
disturbs a reasonable person with continuous or excessive noise.
   RESTRAINT. Confinement within the property of the owner or securing by a
lead or leash.
   STRAY. Any animal whose owner cannot be identified following reasonable
inquiry.
   VICIOUS ANIMAL. Any animal constituting an immediate and serious danger to
humans or to other animals.
(Prior Code, § 90.01) (Ord. 391, passed 3-8-1983)
Statutory reference:
   Construction, see I.C. 15-17-1-2
   Definition of domestic animal, see I.C. 15-17-2-26
   Definition of person, see I.C. 15-17-2-83
§ 90.02 ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER; ENFORCEMENT.
   (A)   (1)   The Office of the Animal Control Officer is herewith created.
The Animal Control Officer shall be appointed by the Town Council and shall
carry out and supervise the enforcement of this chapter.
      (2)   The Office shall be within the Town Police Department, and the
salary shall be fixed by the town and approved by the Town Council.
   (B)   The provisions of this chapter shall be enforced by the Animal Control
Officer and by appropriate law enforcement agencies.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008)
§ 90.03 MOTOR VEHICLE ACCIDENTS INVOLVING DOGS AND CATS.
   Any person who, as the operator of a motor vehicle, strikes a dog or cat
shall stop at once and immediately report the injury or death to the dog or
cat’s owner. In the event the owner cannot be ascertained or located, the
operator shall at once report the accident to the appropriate law enforcement
agency or to the Animal Control Officer.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.04 OWNER RESPONSIBILITY FOR ANIMAL ATTACKS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for an owner or keeper of a dog or cat to allow
that dog or cat to attack and injure a person who did not provoke the dog or
cat prior to the attack.
   (B)   Owners of rental property are responsible for any dog or cat harbored
on their property. In the event a problem arises with a tenant in the
enforcement of this chapter, the owner of the rental property shall assist the
town in said enforcement. If the property owner fails to assist with the
enforcement of this chapter, the property owner may become responsible and
cited into court in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
   (C)   It shall be a defense to prosecution under this section if:
      (1)   The attack occurred in an enclosure in which the animal was
confined without means of escape, there was posted at the main entrance of the
enclosure a notice to beware the dog or cat and the person attacked entered the
enclosure without invitation; or
      (2)   The person was attacked during the commission or attempted
commission of a criminal act on the property of the owner or keeper of the dog
or cat.
   (D)   The liability imposed by this section shall not reduce, substitute for
or in any manner be deemed to be in derogation of the rights accorded victims
of dog bite injury or property damages as provided for in I.C. 15-20-1-3 et
seq., by any successor statutes or by common law.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.05 INCITING DOGS TO FIGHT.
   No person shall incite or cause dogs to fight.
(Prior Code, § 90.03) (Ord. 331, passed 5-7-1963; Ord. 391, passed 3-8-1983)
Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.06 POISONING ANIMALS.
   No person shall expose any known poisonous substance, whether mixed with
food or not, so that the same shall be liable to be eaten by a dog or cat,
provided that it shall not be unlawful for a person to expose on his or her own
property common rat or mouse poison, mixed with vegetable substances or
unmixed.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.07 GIVING ANIMALS AS PRIZES.
   No person shall give away any live animal, fish, reptile or bird as a prize
for or as an inducement to enter any contest, game or other competition, or as
an inducement to enter a place of amusement, or offer the vertebrate as an
incentive to enter into any business agreement whereby the offer was for the
purpose of attracting trade.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.08 LIVESTOCK AND EXOTIC ANIMALS.
   (A)   No person shall have or keep any goat, sheep, pig, hog or other swine,
horse, mule, pony, cattle, duck, goose, turkey, guinea or any other species of
livestock, farm animal or fowl, including, but not limited to, any llama or
ostrich, within the town limits. No person shall present or have in a public
place or a place of public resort any reptile or amphibian unless securely
contained in a cage or similar device.
   (B)   A land owner of at least four acres of land within the town limits may
keep up to four horses or ponies, but not more than four horses or ponies
total, on that land as long as they are properly restrained by effective
fencing and enclosures.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008; Ord. 525, passed 7-7-2015) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.09 CHICKENS.
   (A)   Chickens shall be allowed to be kept within the town limits in
accordance with the following requirements:
      (1)   Not more than six chickens;
      (2)   There shall be no roosters kept within the town limits;
      (3)   Permits required; residents are required to obtain a permit for
keeping backyard chickens, which involves submitting an application and paying
any associated fees of $5 annually;
      (4)   Coops and runs must be predator-proof, well-ventilated and cleaned
to prevent disease and pest infestations;
      (5)   Adequate space for the number of chickens kept should be provided;
each chicken should have at least two square feet of space in the coop and a
minimum of ten square feet of space in the run;
      (6)   Coops need to be 50 feet from neighboring homes and ten feet from
the property lines;
      (7)   Chickens must be kept in the run or coop from daylight to dusk, or
confined by a mobile chicken tractor within the boundaries stated previously;
      (8)   Maintaining clean and sanitary conditions in chicken coops and runs
is essential, with proper waste disposal and regular cleaning required;
      (9)   Chickens must be provided with a clean and sanitary environment,
including clean water and food;
      (10)   Chickens must be provided adequate shelter from the elements;
      (11)   The town may conduct periodic inspections of chicken coops to
ensure compliance with regulations; and
      (12)   Processing is to be out of public view.
   (B)   Failure to uphold these guidelines shall be enforced by those persons
or agencies designated by the municipal authority. It shall be a violation of
this chapter to interfere with an officer in the performance of his or her
duties. Interference is presumed when the owner, keeper, harboror or possessor
of an animal refuses entry to an Animal Control Officer or police officer, or
who refuses to surrender the animal on demand to the officer.
(Ord. 2024-2, passed 4-10-2024) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.10 DISPOSITION OF FUNDS.
   (A)   All fees or monies collected shall be paid to the Clerk/Treasurer or
Animal Control Officer.
   (B)   Money so paid shall be transmitted to the Clerk/Treasurer, shall be
placed in a special fund and shall be used in carrying out the provisions of
this chapter.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008)
LICENSING AND VACCINATION; RABIES CONTROL
§ 90.25 LICENSE REQUIRED.
   (A)   No person shall harbor a dog or cat within the town without first
obtaining the required license.
   (B)   A license shall be issued only after payment of the applicable fees
and the receipt of all application materials. Fees shall be as follows.
Type of Animal License Fee Per Animal
Type of Animal       License Fee Per Animal
Neutered male cat    $3
Neutered male dog    $3
Spayed female cat    $3
Spayed female dog    $3
Un-neutered male cat $3
Un-neutered male dog $5
Un-spayed female cat $3
Un-spayed female dog $5
 
   (C)   A duplicated license may be obtained for a fee of $1. No person shall
use any license for any dog or cat other than the dog or cat for which it was
issued.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.26 TAGS AND IDENTIFICATION COLLARS.
   Upon acceptance of the license application and fee, the Animal Control
Officer shall issue durable tags and identification collars, stamped with an
identifying number and the date of issuance. Dogs and cats must wear tags at
all times when off the premises of the owner. The licensing agent shall
maintain a record of the identifying number of all tags issued.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008)
§ 90.27 DOG OR CAT TO WEAR LICENSE TAG.
   (A)   No person harboring a licensed dog or cat shall permit the dog or cat
to run at large within the town without a substantial collar of leather, iron,
copper, brass or other durable material to which shall be attached its numbered
license tag.
   (B)   No person shall permit any dog or cat to wear any other tag than the
one issued by the town for that dog or cat.
(Prior Code, § 90.17) (Ord. 391, passed 3-8-1983; Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008)
Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.28 REMOVAL OF LICENSE TAG.
   No person other than the owner of the dog or cat shall remove either the
collar or the license tag from any licensed dog or cat except with the consent
of or upon the order of the party to whom the license was issued.
(Prior Code, § 90.18) (Ord. 391, passed 3-8-1983; Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008)
Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.29 EXHIBITION OF LICENSE REQUIRED UPON REQUEST.
   No person shall refuse to exhibit any license required by this subchapter to
any town official, police officer or law enforcement agency.
(Prior Code, § 90.19) (Ord. 391, passed 3-8-1983; Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008)
Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.30 REGISTRATION OF DOGS OR CATS REQUIRED.
   Any person harboring any dog or cat shall, on or before the first Monday in
May of each year, have the dog or cat registered in the office of the Animal
Control Officer and shall pay on or before that time the dog or cat tax levied
by the town.
(Prior Code, § 90.16) (Ord. 391, passed 3-8-1983; Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008)
Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.31 RABIES VACCINATION REQUIRED.
   No person shall harbor any dog or cat which is six months or older and which
has not been vaccinated against rabies. A rabies vaccination tag issued by a
licensed veterinarian; an identification tag designating the owner of the dog
or cat and the owner’s address; and a dog or cat tag issued by the Animal
Control Officer shall be deemed proof of compliance with this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 90.20) (Ord. 391, passed 3-8-1983; Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008)
Penalty, see §
90.99
IMPOUNDMENT; ADOPTION
§ 90.45 RUNNING AT LARGE; RESTRAINING ANIMALS; IMPOUNDMENT PROCEDURES.
   (A)   All animals shall be kept under restraint. No owner shall fail to
exercise due care and control of his or her dog or cat to prevent them from
becoming a public nuisance. Every female dog or cat in heat shall be confined
in a building or secured enclosure in a manner that the female animal cannot
come into contact with another animal of the same species except for planned
breeding. Every vicious animal, as determined by the Animal Control Officer,
shall be confined by the owner within a building or secured enclosure and shall
be securely muzzled or caged whenever off of the premises of the owner.
   (B)   Unrestrained and nuisance animals shall be taken by the police or
Animal Control Officer and impounded in the Town Animal Shelter, and there
confined in a humane manner. If, by a license tag or other means, the owner of
an impounded animal can be identified, the Animal Control Officer shall
immediately, upon impoundment, notify the owner by telephone or mail. Any
animal not reclaimed by its owner within three working days shall become the
property of the local government authority and shall be placed for adoption in
a suitable home or humanely euthanized.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.46 HOLDING OF ANIMALS; FEES, CHARGES AND EXPENSES.
   (A)   Dogs shall be held for not more than three days at the town facility,
and if not claimed within three days from the date the dog is placed in the
town facility, the animal is to be taken to the Anderson Animal Shelter.
   (B)   (1)   The owner and/or owners of a dog held at the town facility, in
order to retrieve the dog, shall pay a fee to the Town Clerk/Treasurer
according to the following schedule:
         (a)   The owner shall pay a fee of $120 to the town to reimburse the
town for the cost of taking the dog to the Anderson Animal Shelter; and
         (b)   In addition, the owner shall pay the following:
            1.   First offense: $50;
            2.   Second offense: $75; and
            3.   Third offense: $100.
      (2)   Every owner with three offenses shall be cited into court for said
violation. If the first or second offense results in personal injury or
property damage, the owner will be cited into court for said violation.
   (C)   If a court requires a dog to be held for more than three days, the
owner shall be charged $15 per day for each day the animal is held.
(Prior Code, § 90.25) (Ord. 391, passed 3-8-1983; Ord. 482, passed 7-2-2001;
Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008; Ord. 511, passed 2-21-2012)
§ 90.47 ADOPTION OF DOGS AND CATS.
   The Animal Control Officer, with the approval of the Town Council, may
promulgate policies and regulations for the adoption of dogs and cats from the
Animal Control Officer.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008)
KENNELS
§ 90.60 KENNEL PERMIT REQUIRED; PROCEDURE.
   (A)   No person shall operate a kennel without first obtaining a permit in
compliance with this subchapter. Each facility regulated by this subchapter
shall be considered a separate enterprise and shall require an individual
permit. No kennel shall be allowed to hold more than seven animals. A kennel
license is required for anyone holding more than two animals.
   (B)   The applicant must apply to the town or Town Planning Commission for a
special exception to operate kennels on his or her property. Applicants must
meet all of the requirements for a kennel. Then, the applicant must submit a
full set of prints showing kennel sites, the construction of kennels and the
location of kennels on the site plans for approval of the Zoning Board.
   (C)   (1)   After the kennel is approved by the town or Town Planning
Commission, the applicant must submit the approved form to the Clerk/Treasurer
for the proper kennel license. The licenses are good for the calendar year in
which they are written for the person or persons receiving approval and must be
renewed by January 31 of the following year.
      (2)   The special exception is good for the person or persons to whom it
is written only, and change of ownership requires a new kennel license.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.61 KENNEL PERMIT FEES.
   (A)   Kennel permit fees are as follows.
 
Number of Accommodated Animals                                 Fees Per Permit
For each kennel authorized to accommodate 7 animals or less    $100
 
   (B)   No fee shall be required of any veterinary hospital, animal shelter or
government-operated zoological park or laboratory.
(Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008)
§ 90.62 KENNEL REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   All kennels will be kept in a sanitary condition. Dog runs will be
hard-surfaced for easy cleaning. All animals will be separated except for
mating or tending young.
   (B)   Kennels shall be separated from the nearest residence or business by
not less than 200 feet.
   (C)   Kennels shall not have over seven animals.
(Ord. 391, passed 3-8-1983; Ord. 458, passed 12-15-1998; Ord. 482, passed 7-2-
2001; Ord. 525, passed 3-18-2008)
§ 90.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   This chapter shall be enforced by the Police Department and
appropriate law enforcement agencies. Any person who violates any provision of
this chapter shall be fined a sum not to exceed $2,500. Each day a violation
continues constitutes a separate offense.
   (B)   A person who violates any provision of §
90.04 of this chapter shall be imposed a fine for any such violation of not
less than $500. If the violation results in the dog or cat causing serious
bodily injury to any person, the court, upon request, shall order the dog or
cat forfeited and/or destroyed.
   (C)   Permits may be revoked, and chickens confiscated, and fees may accrue
in the amount of $25 per violation as set out in §
90.09 of this chapter. Outlined violations in excess of two warnings may result
in the confiscation of chickens, at which point the animals will be placed for
adoption.
(Prior Code, § 90.99) (Ord. 331, passed 5-7-1963; Ord. 391, passed 3-8-1983;
Ord. 2024-2, passed 4-10-2024)
CHAPTER 91: ABANDONED VEHICLES
Section
   
91.01   Definitions
   
91.02   Abandonment of vehicles
   
91.03   Leaving abandoned vehicle on the street
   
91.04   Vehicles not deemed abandoned
   
91.05   Tagging abandoned vehicle or parts
   
91.06   Officer’s abandoned vehicle report
   
91.07   Disposition of abandoned vehicle
 
   
91.99   Penalty
§ 91.01 DEFINITIONS.
   The following definitions shall apply in the interpretation and enforcement
of this chapter.
   ABANDONED VEHICLE. The following:
      (1)   A vehicle located on public property illegally;
      (2)   A vehicle left on public property without being removed for 24
hours;
      (3)   A vehicle located on public property in such a manner as to
constitute a hazard or objection to the movement of pedestrian or vehicular
traffic on a public right-of-way;
      (4)   A vehicle that has remained on private property without the consent
of the owner or person in control of that property can be towed immediately;
      (5)   A vehicle from which the engine, transmission or differential has
been removed or that is otherwise partially dismantled or inoperable and left
on public property;
      (6)   A vehicle that has been removed by a towing service or public
agency upon the request of an officer enforcing a statute or an ordinance if
the impounded vehicle is not claimed or redeemed by the owner or the owner’s
agent within 20 days after the vehicle’s removal;
      (7)   A vehicle that is mechanically inoperable and is left on private
property continuously in a location visible from public property for more than
ten days. A vehicle covered by a tarpaulin or other plastic, vinyl, rubber,
cloth or textile covering is considered to be visible; or
      (8)   A vehicle that has been repaired or stored at the request of the
owner, that has not been claimed by the owner, for which the reasonable value
of the charges associated with the repair or storage remain unpaid for more
than 30 days after the date on which the repair work is completed or the
vehicle is first stored.
   STREET or HIGHWAY. The entire width between the boundary lines of every way
publicly maintained when any part thereof is open to the use of the public for
the purposes of vehicular travel.
   VEHICLE. A machine propelled by power, other than human power, designed to
travel along the ground by use of wheels, treads, runners or slides, and which
transports persons or property or pulls machinery, and shall include, without
limitation, automobiles, trucks, trailers, motorcycles and tractors.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 5-8-2024)
§ 91.02 ABANDONMENT OF VEHICLES.
   (A)   No person shall abandon any vehicle within the corporate boundaries of
the town and no person shall leave any vehicle at any place within the town for
such time and under such certain circumstances so as to cause such vehicle
reasonably to appear to have been abandoned.
   (B)   An abandoned vehicle, under this chapter, shall also be a nuisance.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 5-8-2024) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.03 LEAVING ABANDONED VEHICLE ON THE STREET.
   No person shall leave any abandoned, partially dismantled, non-operating,
wrecked or junked vehicle on any street or highway within the town.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 5-8-2024) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.04 VEHICLES NOT DEEMED ABANDONED.
   This chapter shall not apply to the following:
   (A)   A vehicle in an enclosed building;
   (B)   A vehicle on the premises of a business enterprise operated in a
lawful place and manner when necessary to the operating of such business
enterprise, except those vehicles that have been repaired and stored on the
property for over 30 days as per the definitions;
   (C)   A vehicle in an appropriate junkyard or scrap yard maintained in town;
   (D)   A vehicle located on a vehicle sale lot;
   (E)   A vehicle stored as the property of a member of the armed forces of
the United States who is on active-duty assignment; or
   (F)   A vehicle registered, operable and licensed as an antique vehicle.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 5-8-2024)
§ 91.05 TAGGING ABANDONED VEHICLE OR PARTS.
   The Police Chief or any member of the Police Department who finds or is
notified that a vehicle or parts is believed to be abandoned shall attach in a
prominent place a notice tag containing the following information:
   (A)   The date, the time, the officer’s name and the Police Department’s
address and telephone number to contact for more information;
   (B)   The vehicle or parts are considered abandoned;
   (C)   The vehicle or parts will be removed after 72 hours;
   (D)   The person who owns the vehicle will be held responsible for all costs
incidental to the removal, storage and disposal of the vehicle; and
   (E)   The person who owns the vehicle may avoid costs by removal of the
vehicle or parts within 72 hours.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 5-8-2024)
§ 91.06 OFFICER’S ABANDONED VEHICLE REPORT.
   If a vehicle or parts tagged under §
91.05 of this chapter is not removed within the 72-hour period, the Police
Chief or any member of the Police Department shall prepare a written abandoned
vehicle report of the vehicle or parts, including information on the condition,
missing parts and other facts that might substantiate the estimated market
valve of the vehicle or parts. Photographs shall be taken to describe the
condition of the vehicle or parts.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 5-8-2024)
§ 91.07 DISPOSITION OF ABANDONED VEHICLE.
   (A)   In the event a vehicle or part tagged under §
91.06 of this chapter is not removed within the 72-hour period, and if, in the
opinion of the Police Chief or any member of the Police Department, the market
value of an abandoned vehicle or parts is less than $500, the Police Chief, or
any member of the Police Department, shall make a reasonable effort to
ascertain the person who owns the vehicle or parts, or who may be in control of
the vehicle or parts, and then shall immediately dispose of the vehicle to an
automobile scrap yard. A copy of the abandoned vehicle report and photographs
relating to the abandoned vehicle shall be forwarded to the State Bureau of
Motor Vehicles.
   (B)   (1)   In the event the market value of the abandoned vehicle or parts
is at least $500, the Police Chief, or any member of the Police Department,
before placing a notice tag on the vehicle or parts, shall make a reasonable
effort to ascertain the person who owns the vehicle or parts, or who may be in
control of the vehicle or parts. After 72 hours, the Police Chief or any member
of the Police Department shall require the vehicle or parts to be towed to a
storage area.
      (2)   Said vehicle shall be impounded until lawfully claimed and
reasonable towing and storage charges are paid, or otherwise disposed of in
accordance with state law.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 5-8-2024)
§ 91.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be
fined. The fine for the first offense is $250, for the second offense $500 and
for the third and each subsequent offense $1,000.
   (B)   In the event the town is required to file an action in the County
Court System to enforce the fine and/or seek removal of the vehicle from the
public or private property, or to seek abatement of a nuisance, the owner of
the vehicle shall be responsible for the attorney fees and court costs
associated with the enforcement action.
   (C)   In addition to any other penalty herein, the town may take such civil
action provided by law, including, but not limited to, injunctive relief,
abatement of a nuisance or imposition of a fine which shall serve as a lien on
the vehicle for the recovery of expenses.
(Ord. 2024-3, passed 5-8-2024)
