GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 92.01 STATE LAW ADOPTED.
   (A)   The town adopts the provisions of I.C. 36-7-10.1 and any changes
subsequently made to that statute by the State Legislature.
   (B)   The town adopts the provisions of I.C. 36-7-9 (Chapter 9: Unsafe
Building Law), and specifically adopts the definition of SUBSTANTIAL PROPERTY
INTEREST as set forth in I.C. 36-7-9-2.
   (C)   In compliance with I.C. 36-7-9-3, the town designates the Building
Commissioner as the executive official responsible for the administration and
enforcement of the provisions of the unsafe buildings sections of this chapter
and the aforementioned statute.
   (D)   The Police Department shall have the authority to enforce all other
provisions of this chapter, including §§
92.15 through
92.18. Nothing in this chapter shall be read to limit or restrict the authority
of the Police Department or other law enforcement organization to act to
enforce the law or to investigate civil and criminal violations, including
those having to do with unsafe buildings, dangerous conduct or the use or
possession of property.
   (E)   To the extent these statutes, including any subsequent amendments, may
confer upon the town greater or broader powers to regulate the subject matter
of this chapter, or provide for other or additional enforcement mechanisms from
those set forth in this chapter, state law shall control and the town and its
designated executive may elect to proceed under those methods or to exercise
those powers with proper notice to all affected persons.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024)
§ 92.02 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   PROPERTY OWNER. The recorded owner(s) of a particular property as reflected
by the most current properly records of the county.
   SUBSTANTIAL PROPERTY INTEREST. Any right in real property that may be
affected in a substantial way by actions authorized by this chapter, including
a fee interest, a life estate interest, a future interest, a mortgage interest
or an equitable interest of a contract ordinance.
   QUIET TIMES. Shall be Sunday through Thursday, 11:00 p.m. to 7:00 a.m.; and
Friday and Saturday, 12:00 a.m. (midnight) to 7:00 a.m.
   UNREASONABLE NOISE. Depends in part on the day of the week and time of day.
During QUIET TIMES, any audible or disturbing noise, including music, affecting
people outside the dwelling unit or premises shall be considered UNREASONABLE
NOISE, except in emergencies or as strictly necessary. At all other times,
UNREASONABLE NOISE shall be that which exceeds reasonable limits so as to
significantly disrupt the peace and the activities of others and which is not
required by lawful activities or specifically permitted or allowed by law.
   VEGETATION. Does not include wetlands, woods, nature preserves, undeveloped
areas, stormwater best management practice areas or agricultural crops,
including hay and pasture. VEGETATION does include weed, grasses and other
plants that have died or are no longer growing but have not yet been cut down
and removed.
   WEEDS AND RANK VEGETATION. Any grass, weeds or other rank or useless
vegetation which exceeds the height of eight inches; provided, however, that
such definition does not include:
      (1)   Trees, bushes or shrubs which have been planted or cultivated by
the owner or occupant of the land, and which do not interfere with public
safety or the lawful use of public rights-of-way or easements;
      (2)   Agricultural crops, including ground cover planted or cultivated
for an agricultural purpose; or
      (3)   Vegetation cultivated in plant beds.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024)
REMOVAL OF WEEDS AND RANK VEGETATION
§ 92.15 PUBLIC NUISANCE.
   This subchapter governs the abatement, control and removal of weeds and rank
vegetation, which are hereby declared a public nuisance.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024)
§ 92.16 DUTY OF PROPERTY OWNER.
   It shall be the duty of any owner of real estate within the geographical
limits of the town to cut and remove all weeds and rank vegetation growing upon
such real estate when such weeds and rank vegetation exceed the height of eight
inches, as measured from the ground, including, but not limited to, that
portion of such real estate as is adjacent to or abutting upon any sidewalk,
alley or street.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.17 FAILURE TO CUT; NOTICE; CONTINUOUS ABATEMENT.
   Should any owner of real property with the geographical limits of the town
fail to perform the duties set forth in §
92.16 or any other duties regarding the removal of weeds and rank vegetation
required by law, the town shall serve, in the manner set forth herein below or
by any other means provided by state law, a notice of violation (“notice”), in
the form described herein below.
   (A)   Service of the notice shall be made upon the property owner by mail or
by a member of the Police Department, by the Building Commissioner or other
town officer authorized by the Town Council, by regular or certified mail or
shall be made by equivalent service permitted by I.C. 1-1-7-1 to the owner of
record of the property with a single owner, or at least one of the owners of
record of the property if the property has multiple owners. Service shall be
made to the last address of the owner(s) as indicated in the records of the
County Auditor.
   (B)   The notice shall contain the following information:
      (1)   It shall require the cutting and removal of weeds and rank
vegetation;
      (2)   It shall describe, to the extent necessary and practical, the weeds
and rank vegetation that must be cut and removed;
      (3)   It shall set a time limit for the action to be taken of not less
than ten days from the service of the notice;
      (4)   It shall contain a reference to this chapter and to I.C. 36-7-10.1;
      (5)   It shall set forth the penalties for violation of the ordinance;
and
      (6)   It shall provide a person or a department and contact information
for the owner to contact with any questions.
   (C)   The notice may also contain or be served with a continuous abatement
notice, which serves as notice to the real property owner(s) that each
subsequent violation of this chapter during the same calendar year in which the
initial notice was provided may be abated without further notice by the town or
its contractors and the cost of that abatement assessed to the property owner
(s). If the notice is served by mail, whether regular first class mail,
certified mail or by equivalent service under I.C. 1-1-7-1, a continuous
abatement notice shall also be posted at the property.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.18 REMOVAL BY TOWN; PAYMENT OF COSTS.
   (A)   From the date the notice of violation is mailed, the property owner(s)
has ten days, or such other longer period set forth in the notice, to abate the
violation.
   (B)   After this period has expired, the town will perform a site
inspection. This inspection may be performed by a member of the Police
Department, the Building Inspector or another officer designated and authorized
by the Town Council.
      (1)   If the property owner has abated the violation by removing the
weeds and rank vegetation, the town will note in its records that the property
owner has come into compliance and no further action will be taken except in
the case of subsequent violations as set forth herein.
      (2)   If the property owner fails to abate the violation, the town will
document the violation photographically and take action to do so itself. This
action shall also be documented by before and after photographs and those
records maintained.
   (C)   If the property owner has failed to abate the violation within the
applicable time limit set forth in the notice, the owner shall be liable for
the following fees and costs, in addition to the fines set forth in §
92.99.
      (1)   Administrative fee. To defray the cost to the town of the time,
effort and costs of inspecting the properties, evaluating ownership records and
issuing
notice to the property owners, an administrative fee of $200 shall be charged.
      (2)   Costs of abatement. To defray the costs of equipment and labor
associated with entering the property and removing the weeds and rank
vegetation, the property owner shall be charged a fee of $50 per one-half hour,
or any part thereof, for the time spent by town employees or contractors to
abate the violation.
      (3)   Enforcement. Once the town has abated the violation, the Town
Clerk/Treasurer shall prepare a certified statement showing the time spent and
costs of abatement, which shall be promptly served on the property owner by a
member of the Police Department or by certified or registered mail, requiring
that these fees and costs, together with any outstanding fines, be paid to the
Clerk/Treasurer within ten days. If the owner(s) fail to make payment during
this time, the certified copy of the statement shall be filed in the Office of
the County Auditor.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024)
UNSAFE BUILDINGS AND DANGEROUS CONDUCT OR CONDITIONS IN USE OR POSSESSION OF
REAL PROPERTY
§ 92.30 SCOPE.
   This subchapter governs the regulation of unsafe buildings and dangerous or
deleterious conduct in the use or possession of buildings, structures or other
real property within the geographical limits of the town. The provisions of
this subchapter are separate from and in addition to the provisions of §§
92.15 through
92.18, which are limited to the abatement of weeds and rank vegetation, and
other ordinances governing excessive noise or other nuisances. Nothing in this
subchapter shall be construed to alter or confer any additional procedural
rights to property owners or restrict the powers of the town for actions
proceeding under §§
92.15 through
92.18 these other nuisance ordinances.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024)
§ 92.31 UNSAFE BUILDINGS; PUBLIC NUISANCE; HOW DETERMINED.
   (A)   Unsafe buildings are declared a public nuisance.
   (B)   Unsafe buildings include any dwelling, dwelling unit or rooming unit
that has been declared by the Town Council as unfit or dangerous for human
habitation or that pose a significant danger to members of the public at large,
and that therefore need to be secured, significantly repaired or remediated, or
demolished. This determination shall be made in light of the building’s current
physical state and state of repair; defects in drainage, plumbing, ventilation,
foundation, roof or construction defects; infection with contagious disease or
mold; infestation with vermin; or existence on the premises of an unsanitary
condition, such as to create a hazard to the health, safety and welfare of the
occupants or the public. The Council may also consider whether it is possible
or economically feasible to repair or remediate the dwelling. In addition, any
vacant building shall be declared unfit for human habitation and therefore
unsafe, when its existence, in the judgment of the Council, is detrimental to
the public health, safety and welfare.
   (C)   Any structure, residential, commercial or otherwise, that is so
unsound, unstable or in danger of collapse, whether whole or partial, or
weakened to an extent that it may not be able to resist the forces of nature,
including without limitation, windstorm, rain, snow, hail or earthquake, such
that it poses a danger to occupants or member of the public may be declared an
unsafe building.
   (D)   A building, structure or any condition of property that constitutes an
attractive nuisance, whether to children, or to those who may occupy or use the
premises for criminal purposes, may be declared an unsafe building or premises.
   (E)   This chapter also incorporates by reference the definitions of unsafe
building and unsafe premises contained in I.C. 36-7-9-4. Any building or part
of a building or structure meeting those definitions shall also be considered
an unsafe building or unsafe premises and shall be subject to the procedures,
remedial provisions, and fees and penalties set forth in that statute and this
chapter.
   (F)   The Town Council may adopt by ordinance other and more specific rules
and standards, not inconsistent with this chapter and state law, to supplement
this chapter and to aid in the determination of whether a building is unsafe or
unfit for human habitation. These standards may include construction and
maintenance standards to the extent these endanger the life, health, safety or
property of its occupants or the public.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.32 OTHER DANGEROUS CONDITIONS OR CONDUCT WITH REGARD TO USE OR POSSESSION
OF REAL PROPERTY.
   (A)   The maintenance, depositing, leaving or permitting to be or remain on
any public or private property of any of the following items, conditions or
actions are declared to be a public nuisance; provided, however, that this
enumeration shall not be deemed or constructed, to be conclusive, limiting or
restrictive:
      (1)   Vegetation, trees or woody growth on private property, which, due
to its proximity to any governmental property, right-of-way or easement,
interferes with the public safety or lawful use of the governmental, property,
right-of-way or easement;
      (2)   A condition that causes property to become a health or safety
hazard, unless specifically authorized under existing laws or regulations;
      (3)   Accumulation of rubbish, trash, refuse, junk and other abandoned
materials, metals, lumber or other things;
      (4)   Any condition which provides or may provide harborage for rats,
mice, snakes, insects or other vermin;
      (5)   Any condition that creates a hazard of fire or explosion, including
without limitation the storage of volatile or explosive materials in or around
the property;
      (6)   Any condition involving the release or significant potential for
release of noxious or toxic chemicals, vapors, fumes or substances or which
creates disagreeable or obnoxious odors or stenches;
      (7)   The carcasses of animals or fowl not disposed of within a
reasonable time after death;
      (8)   The pollution of any public well, cistern, stream, lake, canal or
waterway or body of water by sewerage, trash, the remains of dead animals,
creamery or industrial waste, chemicals or any other substance;
      (9)   Any accumulation of stagnant water on any lot or piece of land;
      (10)   Dense smoke noxious fumes, gas, soot or cinder;
      (11)   The unauthorized obstruction of any street, road, alley, sidewalk
or other public way;
      (12)   Any building, structure or other place or local where any activity
which is in violation of local, state or federal law is permitted, conducted,
performed or maintained;
      (13)   Any abandoned vehicle, including without limitation automobiles,
trucks, trailers, campers, boats and campers;
      (14)   Grass clippings, mowed grass, leaves or other vegetation or debris
that are cast, blown or placed onto streets, curbs or alleyways;
      (15)   Unreasonable noise, as defined herein above;
      (16)   Machinery equipment stored on premises that is used, in whole or
part, for residential purposes;
      (17)   Waste, including discarded furniture and appliances, building
materials, tools, toys, automotive or mechanical parts, trash or other refuse,
farm machinery, household fixtures and equipment not in use at the residence,
stored outside of an enclosed building on a residential premises, including a
residence, or enclosed accessory buildings, such as garages, garden sheds or
storage buildings, in other than sanitary containers. All incinerators,
containers, or other materials not kept clean and in sanitary condition shall
also be considered a public nuisance;
      (18)   Any structure not built or manufactured as a permanent residence,
including without limitation automobiles, campers, trailers, RVs, garages,
sheds, storage units and other nonresidential buildings or structures, that is
currently being used as a permanent or long-term residence or has been
continuously occupied as residence of a period of two weeks or more; or
      (19)   Any other condition that, in the sound and reasonable judgment of
the Town Council, constitutes a hazard to occupants of the property, passers-
by, neighbors or members of the general public, not inconsistent with the
provisions of I.C. 36-7-9 et seq. that might endanger the public health safety
or welfare.
   (B)   The determinations to be made under this section may be delegated in
the first instance to the Building Commissioner, another town officer or an
outside contractor or expert specifically designated by the Town Council,
subject to review and final approval by the Town Council.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.33 PROCEDURES FOR DETERMINATION, ADJUDICATION AND REMEDIATION OF UNSAFE
BUILDINGS AND DANGEROUS CONDUCT OR CONDITIONS IN USE OR POSSESSION OF REAL
PROPERTY.
   (A)   Notice to owner and reinspection.
      (1)   Whenever the Town Council or its designee determines that any
dwelling, dwelling unit, rooming unit or other real property or building or
other structure thereon (collectively, hereinafter, premises) violates the
requirements set forth in this subchapter, state law or any applicable rules or
regulations issued pursuant thereto, the Council or its designee shall issue a
notice setting forth the violations and advising the owner, occupant, manager
or other responsible person, or other person with a substantial legal interest
in the property that such violations must be corrected and the condition of the
property remediated.
      (2)   This notice shall:
         (a)   Be in writing;
         (b)   Explain the violations;
         (c)   Describe the premises where the violation occurred;
         (d)   Provide a reasonable time, not to exceed 60 days for the
correction of the violations;
         (e)   Be served as set forth above and in §
92.17(A); and
         (f)   If one or more persons to whom service is addressed cannot be
found after diligent effort to do so, service may be made by posting a notice
in a conspicuous place on the premises or by causing such notice to be
published in a newspaper of general circulation in the county for a period of
two consecutive days.
      (3)   At the end of the time allowed for the correction of violations,
the Town Council or its delegate/designee shall reinspect the premises and
determine whether the violations have been adequately corrected.
   (B)   Second notice of violation.
      (1)   If upon reinspection the violations, in the determination of the
Town Council or its delegate/designee have not been adequately corrected, a
second notice of violation, which shall constitute an order requiring that the
violations shall be corrected within five days shall be issued, if no request
for reconsideration is made to the Town Council or petition for hearing is
filed in a court of competent jurisdiction is filed by the property owner or
other person served by the order.
      (2)   The second notice/order shall be posted in a conspicuous place on
the premises and shall be served in the same manner as the first notice.
      (3)   After the expiration of the time allowed for the request for
reconsideration or hearing has expired, or after the rendering of a decision
adverse to the property owner or other affected person has been made, the
second notice shall be recorded in the Office of the County Recorder. All
subsequent transferees of the premises shall be deemed to have notice of any
second notice so recorded, and shall be subject to and liable for all penalties
and procedures set forth in this chapter and in state law to the same extent as
the original owner or transferor.
      (4)   If the second notice and expiration of the time allowed for
reconsideration or hearing or the rendering of a decision adverse to the
property owner, the town may, through its officers, agents, contractors and
designees, enter the subject property to effect necessary repairs and
remediation to remove the dangerous condition or end the dangerous use; or,
upon compliance with the procedures set forth herein below in this section, to
demolish any unfit or dangerous buildings and structures or dwellings unfit for
human habitation.
   (C)   Orders to vacate dwellings unfit for human habitation.
      (1)   Whenever it is determined by the Town Council or its delegates/
designees that a premises is unfit for human habitation, the Council may issue
an order or notice requiring that all persons dwelling in or occupying the
premises vacate it within 15 days. This may be done before or in place of the
remediation procedures set forth in division (B) above and the demolition
provisions of division (F) below. This notice shall be served in the same
manner as set forth in division (B) above.
      (2)   The Town Council, in making an order to vacate, shall, for good
cause, extend the time within which to comply with the order. The order may be
revoked when the Council is satisfied that the hazard or danger has ceased and
the premises is fit for human habitation.
      (3)   Any owner, occupant, manager or other person in charge of a
dwelling unit or other premises who has received notice of an order to vacate
and has failed to comply with such an order shall be liable for all costs and
expenses paid or incurred by the town, its officers, its agents or its
delegates/designees in executing or otherwise in connection with the order.
These costs and expenses, together with court costs and attorney’s fees, may be
recovered by a civil action brought by the town.
   (D)   Standards for repair work and removal of unsafe buildings and
dangerous conditions. All work performed and materials used in the repair,
remediation or removal of unsafe buildings and dangerous conditions shall be of
good quality and workmanship. Rules and regulations of the State Department of
Fire and Building Services Office of the State Building Commission shall be
considered acceptable practices for purposes of the repair, remediation or
removal of unsafe buildings and dangerous conditions under this chapter.
   (E)   Sealing of unsafe premises. The Town Council or Building Commissioner,
following the procedures set forth in this chapter and state law, including the
emergency provisions of §
92.32, may issue orders sealing unsafe premises against intrusion by
unauthorized persons or the effects whenever either has good cause to believe
that sealing the premises is reasonably necessary to prevent harm to members of
the public other persons, damage to property or interference with repairs or
remedial measures. The Town Council may adopt by separate ordinance specific
standards governing the means that may or are required to be used in sealing
unsafe premises.
   (F)   Demolition of unsafe buildings and other structures.
      (1)   Any building declared unsafe or unfit for human habitation may be
demolished in accordance with the procedures set forth in this chapter and
state law.
      (2)   The owner of any building determined to be unsafe and unrepairable
or unfit for human habitation and therefore in need of demolition, whether such
structure is occupied or vacant, shall be given notice of this determination in
the manner provided for in this chapter and shall be given a reasonable time,
not to exceed 30 days to remove such structure. This time may be extended for
good cause if the building owner provides notice within that period of
intention to remove the structure and outlines a plan, including a reasonable
time table, for doing so.
      (3)   When an owner fails, neglects or refuses to remove the unsafe
building or structure within the required time, the Town Council may apply to a
court of competent jurisdiction for a demolition order. The Court may grant
such order when no request for reconsideration or hearing on the matter is
pending. The cost of demolition shall be recoverable from the owner of the
property or other responsible party in a civil action brought by the Town
Council, which shall enjoy all of the rights of a private creditor.
      (4)   All demolition, whether carried out by the owner or the Town
Council, shall include the filling in of any excavation remaining on the
property on which the demolished structure was located, so as to remove all
potential danger to public health, safety and welfare.
   (G)   Imposition of costs and expenses. The town may recover all reasonable
costs and expenses incurred or paid by the town to secure, repair, remediate,
remove or demolish any unsafe buildings or structures or any dangerous
conditions or uses of the premises. The town may collect these costs and fees
through all means available to private creditors, including, without
limitation, the filing of a collection action in a court of competent
jurisdiction and the execution through all legal means of any judgment entered
in its favor.
   (H)   Reconsideration of notices under this subchapter.
      (1)   Any person affected by a notice under this subchapter or the state
law provisions incorporated herein, by an order to vacate, or by any order
requiring repair, remediation or demolition of a premises, may apply to the
Town Council for reconsider of such notice or order within ten days after it is
issued.
      (2)   The Town Council shall set a time and place for an informal
conference on the matter within five days of the receipt of such application
and shall advise the applicant of that time and place.
      (3)   At the informal conference, the applicant shall be permitted to
present to the Council or one or more of its representatives his or her grounds
for believing that the order should be modified or revoked. Neither the Indiana
Rules of Evidence, the Rules of Civil Procedure or “Robert’s Rules of Order”
shall apply to the informal conference. Any relevant information, including
hearsay, may be presented by the applicant, considered by the Council, and
given the weight that the Council determines appropriate.
      (4)   Following the informal conference, the Council may, in its sole
discretion, request or obtain additional information pertinent to its decision,
which shall be rendered reasonably promptly, but in no event less than 15 days
following the informal conference.
      (5)   Any person aggrieved by the decision of the Town Council may obtain
judicial review by filing in the Circuit or Superior Courts of the county
within five days of notice of the decision a petition requesting that the
decision be set aside in whole or in part. The Council shall file in court a
record of its decision and findings upon notice of the filing of the petition.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024)
§ 92.34 EMERGENCY ORDERS TO SECURE DANGEROUS BUILDINGS AND OTHER STRUCTURES.
   (A)   I.C. 36-7-9-9 authorizes emergency actions regarding unsafe buildings
that may be taken without an order or the giving of notice in order to protect
life, safety or property. The provisions of this statute are incorporated by
reference in this chapter.
   (B)   Under this authority, the Building Inspector or the Police Chief may
take emergency action to seal and secure the unsafe building or structure to
remove any immediate danger, including issuing an order, providing prior notice
or following the other procedures set forth in this chapter, require persons to
vacate the premises and not use it or nearby property and to fence or otherwise
secure the premises against entry until the danger has passed. Any emergency
action by the Building Inspector or Police Chief is subject to expedited review
by the Town Council and may be challenged in a court of competent jurisdiction
by any affected person, as set forth in I.C. 36-7-9-9.
   (C)   The costs of such emergency action may be recovered by court action or
by hearing before the Town Council, in the manner and to the extent set forth
in I.C. 36-7-9-9.
   (D)   Emergency action as authorized and described in this section may be
taken at any time and regardless of whether any other proceedings under this
section are underway or are planned or contemplated.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024)
§ 92.35 UNSAFE BUILDING FUND.
   The town may establish and maintain an Unsafe Building Fund in its operating
budget in accordance with the provisions of I.C. 36-7-9-14 and 36-7-9-15 for
use in the manner and for the purposes of those statutes.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024)
§ 92.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is provided shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   The penalties for a violation of §§
92.15 through
92.18 and notice thereof are listed below and shall be cited into a local
court:
      (1)   First notice received in a calendar year: $100;
      (2)   Second notice received in a calendar year: $200;
      (3)   Third and any subsequent notices received in a calendar year: $400;
and
      (4)   The property owner shall be responsible for these fees regardless
of whether the violation is abated by the property owner or the town, unless
waived by the Town Council upon a showing of hardship or other extraordinary
circumstances.
   (C)   Any person who violates any provisions of §§
92.30 through
92.35 or frustrates, obstructs or interferes with enforcement of any order or
remedial action taken under this chapter or applicable provisions of state law,
including emergency actions under §
92.34, may be fined in amount not to exceed $1,000 per incident. This fine may
be cumulative and be assessed for each day a nuisance is permitted to exist
after notice is received, each day being deemed a separate violation. This fine
shall be in addition to other criminal or civil penalties that may be imposed
by law.
(Ord. 2024-5, passed 7-10-2024)
CHAPTER 93: FIRE PREVENTION AND PROTECTION
Section
   
93.01   Contracts for township fire protection
   
93.02   Open burning prohibited; exception
 
   
93.99   Penalty
§ 93.01 CONTRACTS FOR TOWNSHIP FIRE PROTECTION.
   The Town Council may enter into contracts for providing fire protection for
townships contiguous to and adjoining the town. The contracts shall in no way
diminish the fire protection provided to the residents and taxpayers of the
town. The consideration for such contracts shall be in such amount as the
Council from time to time shall determine.
(Prior Code, § 92.01) (Ord. 352, passed 10-6-1970)
Statutory reference:
   Taxing district, fire protection district deemed municipal corporation, see
I.C. 36-8-11-16
   Township fire protection, see I.C. 36-8-13-1
§ 93.02 OPEN BURNING PROHIBITED; EXCEPTION.
   (A)   OPEN BURNING, as defined by I.C. 14-23-7-5, means the products of
combustion are emitted directly into the surrounding air and are not conducted
into the air through a stack, chimney, duct or pipe. The term includes
aboveground or underground smoldering fires.
   (B)   No person shall openly burn any materials on public or private
property except as specifically authorized by this section. No person shall
allow the accumulation or existence of combustible material that constitutes or
contributes to open burning.
   (C)   Exceptions where open burning is allowed:
      (1)   The burning of untreated, natural wood products, such as tree
limbs, leaves, twigs and branches;
      (2)   Campfires and fires used solely for recreational purposes, where
such fires are properly controlled by a responsible person; and
      (3)   Ceremonial fires and bonfires used in connection with religious
ceremonies, school pep rallies, scouting activities and similar purposes.
   (D)   All open burning must comply with the following conditions.
      (1)   A person who burns any material shall extinguish the fire if the
fire creates a nuisance or fire hazard.
      (2)   Burning may not be conducted during unfavorable meteorological
conditions, such as high winds, temperature inversions or air stagnation.
      (3)   All fires must be attended at all times during burning until
completely extinguished.
      (4)   All burning shall comply with other federal, state and local laws,
rules and ordinances.
   (E)   This section shall be enforced by the Town Marshal.
(Prior Code, § 92.02) (Ord. 398, passed 9-3-1985; Ord. 530, passed 7-8-2008)
Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is provided shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code.
   (B)   (1)   Any person who violates any provision of §
93.02 of this chapter shall be subject to penalties as provided for a Class C
infraction.
      (2)   For the second and/or subsequent occasion that the Summitville-Van
Buren Township Volunteer Fire Department is called to a location to extinguish
a fire that is in violation of §
93.02 of this chapter, the party or parties in possession of the premises where
the fire was required to be extinguished shall be required to pay $25 to help
defray the costs, charges and/or expenses of extinguishing the fire.
      (3)   Said $25 charge is due and payable to the Clerk/Treasurer of the
town within ten days after notice of the claim is sent by the Clerk/Treasurer
by certified mail, return receipt requested, to the post office address of the
party or parties in possession of the premises at the address where the fire
was extinguished.
(Prior Code, § 92.99) (Ord. 398, passed 9-3-1985; Ord. 459, passed 1-20-1999)
CHAPTER 94: FAIR HOUSING
Section
   
94.01   Policy statement
   
94.02   Definitions
   
94.03   Unlawful practice
   
94.04   Discrimination in the sale or rental of housing
   
94.05   Discrimination in residential real estate-related transactions
   
94.06   Discrimination in the provision of brokerage services
   
94.07   Interference, coercion or intimidation
   
94.08   Prevention of intimidation in fair housing cases
   
94.09   Equal access to housing in HUD programs
   
94.10   Exemptions
   
94.11   Administrative enforcement of chapter

§ 94.01 POLICY STATEMENT.
   It shall be the policy of the town to provide, within constitutional
limitation, for fair housing throughout its corporate limits as provided for
under the Federal Civil Rights Act of 1968, being 42 U.S.C. §§ 3601 et seq., as
amended, the Housing and Community Development Act of 1974, being 42 U.S.C. §§
5301 et seq., as amended, and I.C. 22-9.5-1 et seq.
(Ord. 556, passed 5-7-2013)
§ 94.02 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   AGGRIEVED PERSON. Includes any person who (I.C. 22-9.5-2-2):
      (1)   Claims to have been injured by a discriminatory housing practice;
or
      (2)   Believes that such person will be injured by a discriminatory
housing practice that is about to occur.
   COMMISSION. The State Civil Rights Commission created pursuant to I.C. 22-9-
1-4 et seq.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-3)
   COMPLAINANT. A person, including the Commission, filing a complaint under
I.C. 22-9.5-6.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-4)
   DISABILITY.
      (1)   With respect to a person:
         (a)   A physical or mental impairment which substantially limits one
or more of such person’s major life activities;
         (b)   A record of having such an impairment;
         (c)   Being regarded as having such an impairment;
         (d)   An impairment described or defined pursuant to the Federal
Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990, being 42 U.S.C. §§ 12101 et seq.; or
         (e)   Any other impairment defined under I.C. 22-9-5-6.
      (2)   The term DISABILITY shall not include current illegal use of or
addictions to a controlled substance as defined in 21 U.S.C. § 802 (910 I.A.C.
2-3-2(14), I.C. 22-9-5-6(d)(5)); nor does the term DISABILITY include an
individual solely because that individual is a transvestite (910 I.A.C. 2-3-2
(14), I.C. 22-9-5-6(d)(3)). See also 910 I.A.C. 2-3-2(14).
   DISCRIMINATORY HOUSING PRACTICE. An act that is unlawful under §§
94.04 to 94.08 of this chapter or I.C. 22-9.5-5.
   DWELLING. Any building, structure or part of a building or structure that is
occupied as, or designed or intended for occupancy as, a residence by one or
more families; or any vacant land which is offered for sale or lease for the
construction or location of a building, structure or part of a building or
structure that is occupied as, or designed or intended for occupancy as, a
residence by one or more families.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-8)
   FAMILIAL STATUS. Discrimination on the basis of FAMILIAL STATUS means
discrimination because the person is pregnant; domiciled with an individual
under the age of 18 years of age in regard to whom the person is the parent or
legal custodian or has the written permission of the parent or legal custodian
for domicile with that person; or in the process of obtaining legal custody of
an individual younger than 18 years of age.
   FAMILY. Includes a single individual (I.C. 22-9.5-2-9), with the status of
such FAMILY being further defined in “familial status” in this section.
   PERSON. Includes one or more individuals, corporations, partnerships,
associations, legal representatives, labor organizations, joint-stock
companies, mutual companies, non-incorporated organizations, trusts, trustees,
trustees in cases under 11 U.S.C., receivers and fiduciaries.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-11)
   TO RENT. Includes to lease, to sublease, to let and otherwise to grant for a
consideration the rights to occupy the premises not owned by the occupant.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-13)
(Ord. 556, passed 5-7-2013; Ord. 556, passed 1-23-2018)
§ 94.03 UNLAWFUL PRACTICE.
   Subject to the provisions of division (B) below, §
94.10 of this chapter and I.C. 22-9.5-3, the prohibitions against
discrimination in the sale or rental of housing set forth in I.C. 22-9.5-5-
1 and in §
94.04 of this chapter shall apply to:
   (A)   All dwellings except as exempted by division (B) below and I.C. 22-
9.5-3;
   (B)   Other than the provisions of division (C) below, nothing in §
94.04 of this chapter shall apply to:
      (1)   Any single-family house sold or rented by an owner where the
private individual owner does not own more than three such single-family houses
at any one time; provided that in the sale of such single- family house by a
private individual owner not residing in the house at the time of sale or
exemption, such shall apply only to one such sale within any 24-month period.
The private individual owner may not own any interest in, nor have owned or
reserved on his or her behalf, title to or any right to all or a portion of the
proceeds from the sale or rental of more than three such single-family houses
at any one time. The sale or rental of any such single-family house shall be
exempted from the application of this section only if such house is sold or
rented:
         (a)   Without the use in any manner of the sales or rental facilities
or services of any real estate broker, agent or salesperson, or any person in
the business of selling or renting dwellings, or of any employee or agent of
any such broker, agent or salesperson, or person; and
         (b)   Without the publication, posting or mailing, after notice of
advertisement or written notice in violation of §
94.04(C) of this chapter, but noting in this provision shall prohibit the use
of attorneys, escrow agents, abstracters, title companies and other such
professional assistance as necessary to perfect or transfer this title.
      (2)   Rooms or units in dwellings containing living quarters occupied or
intended to be occupied by not more than four families living independently of
each other, if the owner actually maintains and occupies one of such living
quarters as his or her residence.
   (C)   For the purposes of division (B) above, a person shall be deemed to be
in the business of selling or renting dwellings if:
      (1)   He or she has, within the preceding 12 months, participated as
principal in three or more transactions involving the sale or rental of any
dwelling or any interest therein;
      (2)   He or she has, within the preceding 12 months, participated as
agent, other than in the sale of his or her own personal residence, in
providing sales or rental facilities or services in two or more transactions
involving the sale or rental of any dwelling or any interest therein; or
      (3)   He or she is the owner of any dwelling unit designed or intended
for occupancy by, or occupied by, five or more families.
(Ord. 556, passed 5-7-2013)
§ 94.04 DISCRIMINATION IN THE SALE OR RENTAL OF HOUSING.
   As made applicable by §
94.03 of this chapter, and except as exempted by §§
94.03(B) and §
94.10 of this chapter, it shall be unlawful:
   (A)   To refuse to sell or rent, after the making of a bona fide offer, or
to refuse to negotiate for the sale or rental of, or otherwise make unavailable
or deny, a dwelling to any person because of race, color, religion, sex,
disability, familial status or national origin;
   (B)   To discriminate against any person in the terms, conditions or
privileges of sale or rental of a dwelling, or in the provision of services of
facilities in connection therewith, because of race, color, religion, sex,
disability, familial status or national origin;
   (C)   To make, print or publish, or cause to be made, printed or published,
any notice, statement or advertisement, with respect to the sale or rental of a
dwelling, that indicates any preference, limitation or discrimination based on
race, color, religion, sex, disability, familial status or national origin, or
an intention to make any such preference, limitation or discrimination;
   (D)   To represent to any person because of race, color, religion, sex,
disability, familial status or national origin that any dwelling is not
available for inspection, sale or rental when such dwelling is in fact so
available;
   (E)   For profit, to induce or attempt to induce any person to sell or rent
any dwelling by representations regarding the entry or perspective entry into
the neighborhood of a person or persons of a particular race, color, religion,
sex, disability, familial status or national origin;
   (F)   To discriminate in the sale or rental, or to otherwise make
unavailable or deny, a dwelling to any buyer or renter because of a disability
of:
      (1)   The buyer or renter;
      (2)   A person residing in or intending to reside in that dwelling after
it is so sold, rented or made available; or
      (3)   Any person associated with that person.
   (G)   To discriminate against any person in the terms, conditions or
privileges of sale or rental of a dwelling, or in the provision of services or
facilities in connection with such dwelling, because of a disability of:
      (1)   That person;
      (2)   A person residing in or intending to reside in that dwelling after
it is so sold, rented or made available; or
      (3)   Any person associated with that person.
   (H)   (1)   For the purpose of this section, DISCRIMINATION includes:
         (a)   A refusal to permit, at the expense of the disabled person,
reasonable modifications of existing premises occupied or to be occupied by
such person if such modifications may be necessary to afford such person full
enjoyment of the premises, except that in the case of a rental, the landlord or
landlady may, where it is reasonable to do so, condition permission for a
modification on the renter agreeing to restore the interior of the premises to
the condition that existed before the modifications, reasonable wear and tear
excepted;
         (b)   A refusal to make reasonable accommodations in rules, policies,
practices or services when such accommodations may be necessary to afford such
person equal opportunity to use and enjoy a dwelling; or
         (c)   In connection with the design and construction of covered multi-
family dwellings for first occupancy after the date that is 30 months after
September 13, 1998, a failure to design and construct those dwellings in such a
manner that:
            1.   The public use and common use portions of such dwellings are
readily accessible to and usable by disabled persons;
            2.   All the doors designed to allow passage into and within all
premises within such dwellings are sufficiently wide to allow passage by
disabled persons in wheelchairs; and
            3.   All premises within such dwellings contain the following
features of adaptive design:
               a.   An accessible route into and through the dwelling;
               b.   Light, switches, electrical outlets, thermostats and other
environmental controls in accessible locations; and
               c.   Reinforcements inside bathrooms such that an individual in
a wheelchair can maneuver about the space.
      (2)   Compliance with the appropriate requirements of the Americans with
Disabilities Act of 1990, being 42 U.S.C. §§ 12101 et seq. and of the American
National Standard for Buildings and Facilities providing accessibility and
usability for physically disabled people (commonly cited as ANSI A117.1”)
suffices to satisfy the requirements of division (H)(1)(c)3.c. above.
      (3)   Nothing in this section requires that a dwelling be made available
to an individual whose tenancy would constitute a direct threat to the health
or safety of other individuals or whose tenancy would result in substantial
physical damage to the property of others.
(Ord. 556, passed 5-7-2013; Ord. 556, passed 1-23-2018) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.05 DISCRIMINATION IN RESIDENTIAL REAL ESTATE-RELATED TRANSACTIONS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person or other entity whose business
includes engaging in residential real estate-related transactions to
discriminate against any person in making available such a transaction, or in
the terms or conditions of such a transaction, because of race, color,
religion, sex, disability, familial status or national origin.
   (B)   As used in this section, the term RESIDENTIAL REAL ESTATE-RELATED
TRANSACTION means any of the following:
      (1)   The making or purchasing of loans or providing other financial
assistance:
         (a)   For purchasing, constructing, improving, repairing or
maintaining a dwelling; or
         (b)   Secured by residential real estate.
      (2)   The selling, brokering or appraising of residential real property.
   (C)   Nothing in this chapter prohibits a person engaged in the business of
furnishing appraisals of real property to take into consideration factors other
than race, color, religion, national origin, sex, disability or familial
status.
(Ord. 556, passed 5-7-2013) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.06 DISCRIMINATION IN THE PROVISION OF BROKERAGE SERVICES.
   It shall be unlawful to deny any person access to or membership or
participation in any multiple-listing service, real estate brokers’
organization or other service, organization or facility relating to the
business of selling or renting dwellings, or to discriminate against him or her
in the terms or conditions of such access, membership or participation, on
account of race, color, religion, sex, disability, familial status or national
origin.
(Ord. 556, passed 5-7-2013; Ord. 556, passed 1-23-2018) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.07 INTERFERENCE, COERCION OR INTIMIDATION.
   It shall be unlawful to coerce, intimidate, threaten or interfere with any
person in the exercise or enjoyment of, or on account of his or her having
exercised or enjoyed, or on account of his or her having aided or encouraged
any other person in the exercise or enjoyment of, any right granted or
protected by §§
94.03 to 94.06 of this chapter.
(Ord. 556, passed 5-7-2013) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.08 PREVENTION OF INTIMIDATION IN FAIR HOUSING CASES.
   Whoever, whether or not acting under code or law, by force or threat of
force willfully injures, intimidates or interferes with, or attempts to injure,
intimidate or interfere with, the following shall be fined or imprisoned as set
out in §
94.99 of this chapter:
   (A)   Any person because of his or her color, religion, sex, disability,
familial status or national origin, and because he or she has been selling,
purchasing, renting, financing, occupying or contracting or negotiating for the
sale, purchase, rental, financing or occupation of any dwelling, or applying
for or participating in any service, organization or facility relating to the
business of selling or renting dwellings;
   (B)   Any person because he or she has been, or in order to intimidate such
person or any other person or any class of persons from:
      (1)   Participating, without discrimination on account of race, color,
religion, sex, disability, familial status or national origin, in any of the
activities, services, organizations or facilities described in division (A)
above; or
      (2)   Affording another person or class of persons opportunity or
protection so to participate.
   (C)   Any citizen because he or she is or has been, or in order to
discourage such citizen or any other citizen from lawfully aiding or
encouraging other persons to participate without discrimination on account of
race, color, religion, sex, disability, familial status or national origin, in
any of the activities, services, organizations or facilities described in
division (A) above, or participating lawfully in speech or peaceful assembly
opposing any denial of the opportunity to participate.
(Ord. 556, passed 5-7-2013; Ord. 556, passed 1-23-2018) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.09 EQUAL ACCESS TO HOUSING IN HUD PROGRAMS.
   Pursuant to 24 C.F.R. §§ 5.403 and 574.3, the definition of “family” is
revised to include families regardless of the actual or perceived sexual
orientation, gender identity or marital status of its members.
(Ord. 556, passed 1-23-2018)
§ 94.10 EXEMPTIONS.
   (A)   Exemptions defined or set forth under I.C. 22-9.5-3 et seq. shall be
exempt from the provisions of this chapter, to include those activities or
organizations set forth under divisions (B) and (C) below.
   (B)   Nothing in this chapter shall prohibit a religious organization,
association or society, or any nonprofit institution or organization operated,
supervised or controlled by or in conjunction with a religious organization,
association or society, from limiting the sale, rental or occupancy of
dwellings which it owns or operates for other than a commercial purpose to
persons of the same religion, or from giving preference to such persons, unless
membership in such religion is restricted on account of race, color or national
origin. Nor shall anything in this chapter prohibit a private club not in fact
open to the public which, as an incident to its primary purpose or purposes,
provides lodgings which it owns or operates for other than a commercial purpose
from limiting the rental or occupancy of such lodging to its members or from
giving preference to its members.
   (C)   Nothing in this chapter regarding familial status shall apply with
respect to housing for older persons. As used in this section, HOUSING FOR
OLDER PERSONS means housing:
      (1)   Provided under any state or federal program that the Secretary of
the Federal Department of Housing and Urban Development or the State Civil
Rights Commission determines is specifically designed and operated to assist
elderly persons (as defined in the state or federal program);
      (2)   Intended for and solely occupied by persons 62 years of age or
older; or
      (3)   Intended and operated for occupancy by at least one person 55 years
of age or older per unit.
(Ord. 556, passed 5-7-2013; Ord. 556, passed 1-23-2018)
§ 94.11 ADMINISTRATIVE ENFORCEMENT OF CHAPTER.
   (A)   The authority and responsibility for properly administering this
chapter and referral of complaints hereunder to the Commissioner as set forth
in division (B) below shall be vested in the chief elected official of the
town.
   (B)   Notwithstanding the provisions set out in I.C. 22-9.5-4-8, the town,
because of lack of financial and other resources necessary to fully administer
enforcement proceedings and possible civil actions under the chapter, herein
elects to refer all formal complaints of violation of the articles of this
chapter by complainants to the State Civil Rights Commission for administrative
enforcement actions pursuant to I.C. 22-9.5-6, and the chief elected official
of the town shall refer all said complaints to the Commission as provided for
under division (A) above to said Commission for the purposes of investigation,
resolution and appropriate relief as provided for under I.C. 22-9.5-6.
   (C)   All executive departments and agencies of the town shall administer
their departments, programs and activities relating to housing and urban
development in a manner affirmatively to further the purposes of this chapter
and shall cooperate with the chief elected official and the Commission to
further such purposes.
   (D)   The chief elected official of the town, or the chief elected
official’s designee, shall provide information on remedies available to any
aggrieved person or complainant requesting such information.
(Ord. 556, passed 5-7-2013; Ord. 556, passed 1-23-2018)
§ 94.99 PENALTY.
   Whoever violates the provisions of this chapter as set out in §
94.08 of this chapter shall be fined according to local, state and federal law;
and if bodily injury results, shall be fined not more than $10,000 or
imprisoned not more than ten years, or both; and if death results, shall be
subject to imprisonment for any term of years or for life.
(Ord. 556, passed 5-7-2013)
CHAPTER 95: STREETS AND SIDEWALKS
Section
   
95.01   Municipal highway system
§ 95.01 MUNICIPAL HIGHWAY SYSTEM.
   (A)   The Town Council hereby establishes the Municipal Highway System,
consisting of all highways contained in the volume titled “Summitville Road
Inventory.” Two copies of this volume are on file in the office of the Clerk/
Treasurer for public inspection and are incorporated herein by reference.
   (B)   On or before November 1 of each year, the Town Council shall compile a
list of those highways accepted or vacated by the town during the past year. A
copy of this list shall be sent to the County Council of Governments to assist
said Council in promptly obtaining highway assistance funds for the town.
(Prior Code, § 94.01)

CHAPTER 97: SPECIAL EVENTS
Section
   
97.01   Definitions
   
97.02   Permit required
   
97.03   Unlawful to hold special event without permit
   
97.04   Procedure for obtaining permit
   
97.05   Permit denial
   
97.06   Appeal
   
97.07   Intervention by Police Chief or Fire Marshal
   
97.08   Event organizer requirements
   
97.09   Coordination with Police Department and Fire Department
   
97.10   Utility needs
   
97.11   Support from the town
   
97.12   Liability insurance requirements
   
97.13   Adherence to local ordinances
   
97.14   Food vendors and alcoholic beverages
   
97.15   Reservation of annual event dates
§ 97.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   EVENT SPONSOR/COORDINATOR. The person(s), party or entity that organizes a
special event and has applied for a special event permit under this chapter, or
the person(s), party or entity designated as such on a special event permit
application.
   SPECIAL EVENT. A temporary event or gathering, including a parade, using
private or public property that draws an estimated number of participants and
spectators exceeding 150 people present on any day of the event and that
involves one or more of the following activities:
      (1)   Closing of a public street;
      (2)   Blocking or restricting streets, sidewalks, alleys or other public
places, in whole or in part;
      (3)   Sale or distribution of food or beverages on streets, sidewalks,
alleys or other public places or public property, or on private property where
otherwise prohibited by ordinance;
      (4)   Placement of tents, utility poles or other temporary structures on
a street, sidewalk, alley or other public place;
      (5)   Erection or placement of a stage, bandshell, trailer, portable
building, grandstand, bleachers or other apparatus used for entertainment
purposes on public property; or
      (6)   Activity that requires for its successful execution the provision
and coordination of municipal services to a degree significantly over and above
that which the town routinely provides under ordinary circumstances.
   SPECIAL EVENT ZONE. A geographically defined area that the special event
coordinator has designated as where the event will take place.
   TOWN. The Town of Summitville, Indiana.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.02 PERMIT REQUIRED.
   A permit is required for each and every special event held within the town.
The event organizer must follow the procedures in this chapter in order to
obtain a special event permit from the town. The fee for each license is $50,
payable to the town.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.03 UNLAWFUL TO HOLD SPECIAL EVENT WITHOUT PERMIT.
   It shall be deemed unlawful for any person or organizer to engage in the
operation of a special event, or to permit, maintain, promote, conduct,
advertise, undertake, organize, manage, sell or give tickets to an actual or
reasonably anticipated assembly, unless a permit to hold the special event has
first been issued by the town.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 97.04 PROCEDURE FOR OBTAINING PERMIT.
   (A)   The event organizer of any special event requiring a special event
permit shall submit a special event permit application, which can be obtained
from Town Hall, containing the following information to the Town Council not
less than 60 days in advance of the proposed event:
      (1)   Name of event;
      (2)   Type of event, e.g., festival, carnival, assembly, parade and the
like;
      (3)   General event description;
      (4)   Contact information for event organizer and event organizing agency
(if applicable);
      (5)   Contact information for the on-site manger(s) during the event;
      (6)   Documentation confirming the event organization’s status as for-
profit or not-for-profit;
      (7)   Proof of liability coverage and/or insurance to cover the event;
      (8)   Expected or anticipated attendance;
      (9)   Site or building capacity, if applicable;
      (10)   Dates and times, including time to set up and break down and all
cleanup;
      (11)   Layout of the proposed event, including:
         (a)   All food vendor locations;
         (b)   All alcohol vendor locations;
         (c)   Routes for any 5Ks, marches, rallies, races, parades, “poker
runs” and the like; and
         (d)   Any amusement rides or animal rides.
      (12)   Any requested street closures and/or proposed changes in traffic
flows for the event;
      (13)   Identified parking areas where event attendees will be directed
that will adequately accommodate expected event attendance;
      (14)   Description of restroom facilities that will adequately
accommodate expected event attendance;
      (15)   Description of vendors and names of any known vendors;
      (16)   Description of whether or not alcohol will be sold; and
      (17)   The number of police officers required by the Chief of Police.
   (B)   After receiving the application from the event organizer, the Town
Council members shall receive copies of the application from the Town Clerk/
Treasurer.
   (C)   At the next Town Council meeting, the Town Council President shall
allow time on the agenda for the meeting to allow the event organizer a
reasonable period of time to present their special event application to the
Council. This will allow the Town Council and the event organizer a period of
time for questions and answers concerning the event. Specifically, this is the
allowed time for an event organizer to request that the town subsidize any
portion of the municipal or utility costs associated with the special event.
This shall be determined on a case-by-case basis as detailed in §
97.11(B) of this chapter.
   (D)   After review and presentation from the event organizer, the Town
Council shall have a vote on whether or not to issue a special event permit to
the event organizer.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.05 PERMIT DENIAL.
   The town may refuse to issue a special event permit under the following
circumstances:
   (A)   If the special event permit application and accompanying documentation
is incomplete, is insufficient or does not provide information such that the
town can verify conformance with all special event requirements and the event
organizer is unwilling or unable to provide this information;
   (B)   If the special event permit applicant fails to remit the fees for the
administration of the special event permit;
   (C)   If the town determines that it will not be able to ensure public
health and safety during the event; and
   (D)   If the event organizer or organization has a poor record of
conformance with permit requirements.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.06 APPEAL.
   Any entity that is denied a special event permit may appeal that denial to
the Town Council within 30 days of receipt of denial.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.07 INTERVENTION BY POLICE CHIEF OR FIRE MARSHAL.
   The Chief of Police, Fire Marshal or their designee may intervene in the
operation of any special event that poses a clear and present danger to the
participants or the public, or where state or local laws or ordinances are
being violated, regardless of whether the event is properly permitted and
complying with permit requirements. Intervention may include closing the event
if it is necessary in the professional judgment of the Chief of Police or Fire
Marshal.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.08 EVENT ORGANIZER REQUIREMENTS.
   The event organizer must be at least 21 years of age. They must provide a
day-of-event contact. The event organizer is responsible for notifying the Town
Council of any changes in the plans for the special event.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.09 COORDINATION WITH POLICE DEPARTMENT AND FIRE DEPARTMENT.
   Prior to submitting a proposal to the Town Council, the event organizer
shall discuss the proposed special event with the Chief of Police and the Fire
Chief. The Chief of Police will inform the event organizer how many police
officers will be required for the special event. The Fire Chief will confer
will the event organizer if any special precautions or necessary safety
measures need to be put in place regarding the special event.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.10 UTILITY NEEDS.
   If the event organizer needs electricity and/or water for a special event,
the event organizer is responsible for all charges incurred by his or her
special event for the duration of the event. The town shall send the event
organizer a bill for these utilities after the conclusion of the event.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.11 SUPPORT FROM THE TOWN.
   The town will provide municipal service support to special events at three
different levels of support.
   (A)   Fully supported town events. The town will provide full-service
support for special events that are hosted by the town. This shall include the
Summitville Fireworks hosted by the town and the Town Fire Department annually.
It shall be at the Town Council’s discretion to host additional events as fully
supported town events.
   (B)   Partial town-subsidized events. The town may subsidize a portion of
the costs for a special event, e.g., utilities and trash. This reimbursement or
payment for services shall be determined by the Town Council on a case-by-case
basis if the event is considered to be of general interest to the public and
enhances the town’s public image. The event organizer must reimburse the town
for any town costs in excess of the support level authorized by the Town
Council.
   (C)   For-profit events. The town may allow special events operated by for-
profit event organizers. If an event is organized by a for-profit event
organizer, the event organizer(s) shall be responsible to pay 100% of all
municipal service support costs as well as all utilities.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.12 LIABILITY INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   All special events shall require liability coverage provided by the
event organizer.
   (B)   At minimum, each event organizer shall provide coverage limits as
follows:
      (1)   Each occurrence: $1,000,000; and
      (2)   General aggregate: $2,000,000.
   (C)   The event organizer shall provide proof of liability coverage to the
Town Council with the submission of his or her application. The “Town of
Summitville” has to be listed as a certificate holder and an additional
insured, including waiver of subrogation and primary/non-contributory wording.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.13 ADHERENCE TO LOCAL ORDINANCES.
   Event organizers shall ensure that vendors and active participants obey all
local ordinances, except those which may have been waived to accommodate the
event.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.14 FOOD VENDORS AND ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES.
   The event organizer(s) shall comply with the following provisions concerning
food vendors and alcohol:
   (A)   Food venders are required to comply with all County Health Department
rules and regulations for temporary food license facilities. Vendors are
required to contact the County Health Department for the latest rules and
regulations to obtain a temporary food licenses; and
   (B)   Special events that include the furnishing and/or consumption of
alcohol require the event organizer to provide proof of compliance of state
alcoholic beverage laws and regulations as well as the name of the alcohol
permit holder, a copy of the permit and license and proof of insurance.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
§ 97.15 RESERVATION OF ANNUAL EVENT DATES.
   If an event is intended to be an annual event at regularly scheduled dates,
the current year’s application will include reservation of the following year’s
proposed dates. However, the event organizer shall go through the special event
permit process every year. Reserving an annual date shall not constitute
approval of the following year’s or future years’ events. Each year the event
organizer shall timely submit a special event permit application to the Town
Council for approval.
(Ord. 2020-12, passed 2-12-2020)
TITLE XI: BUSINESS REGULATIONS
   Chapter

§ 110.01 LIQUOR RETAILER PERMITS.

(Prior Code, § 110.01) (Ord. 355, passed 5-9-1972)
