GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 154.001 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ACCESSORY USE OR STRUCTURE. A use or structure on the same lot with, and of
a nature customarily incidental and subordinate to, the principal use or
structure.
   ALTERATIONS, STRUCTURAL. Any change in the supporting members of a building,
such as bearing walls, columns, beams or girders.
   AUTOMOTIVE, MOBILE HOME, TRAILER AND FARM IMPLEMENT SALES. The sale or
rental of new and used motor vehicles, mobile homes, trailers or farm
implements, but not including repair work except incidental warranty repair of
the same to be displayed and sold on the premises. An incidental warranty
repair of the same shall be displayed and sold on the premises.
   AUTOMOTIVE REPAIR. The repair, rebuilding or reconditioning of motor
vehicles or parts thereof, including collision service and the painting and
steam cleaning of vehicles.
   AUTOMOTIVE WRECKING. The dismantling or wrecking of used motor vehicles,
mobile homes or trailers, or the storage, sale or dumping of dismantled,
partially dismantled, obsolete or wrecked vehicles or their parts.
   BUILDING. Any structure designed or intended for the support, enclosure,
shelter or protection of persons, animals, chattels or property.
   BUILDING COMMISSIONER. The official designated by the Council and authorized
to enforce this chapter.
   BUILDING, HEIGHT. The vertical distance measured from the average elevation
of the proposed finished grade at the front of the building to the highest
point of the roof for flat roofs, and to the deck line of mansard roofs, and
the mean height between eaves and ridge for gable, hip and gambrel roofs.
   CERTIFICATE OF OCCUPANCY. A certificate signed by the Building Commissioner
stating that the occupancy and use of land or a building or structure referred
to therein complies with the provisions of this chapter.
   CLINIC. A place used for the care, diagnosis and treatment of sick, ailing,
infirm or injured persons, and those who are in need of medical and surgical
attention, but who are not provided with board or room or kept overnight on the
premises.
   CLUB. A building, or portion thereof, or premises owned or operated by a
person for a social, literary, political, educational or recreational purpose
primarily for the exclusive use of members and their guests.
   COMMISSION. The Town Plan Commission.
   DWELLING, INDUSTRIALIZED UNIT. An assembly of materials or products
comprising all or part of a total structure which, when constructed, is self-
sufficient or substantially self-sufficient, and when installed, constitutes a
dwelling unit, except for necessary preparations for its placement.
   DWELLING, MOBILE HOME. House trailers; a detached dwelling unit designed to
be repeatedly transported on highways, and when arriving at the site for
placement, involving only minor and incidental unpacking, assembling and
connection operations; but which involves no substantial reconstruction which
would render the unit unfit as a conveyance on the highway. The unit shall be
considered as real property if such reconstruction is undertaken and a
permanent foundation is connected to all town utilities.
   DWELLING UNIT. Space within a building comprising a living, dining and
sleeping room or rooms, and storage closets, as well as space and equipment for
cooking, bathing and toilet facilities, all used by only one family and its
household employees.
   FAMILY. One or more persons occupying a single-dwelling unit, provided that
unless all members are related by blood, adoption or marriage, no such family
shall contain over five persons.
   FLOOR AREA OF A RESIDENTIAL BUILDING. The sum of the gross horizontal area
of the several floors of a residential building, excluding basement floor areas
not devoted to residential use, but including the area of roofed porches and
roofed terraces. All dimensions shall be measured between interior faces of
walls.
   GARAGE, PRIVATE. A detached accessory building or portion of a principal
building for the parking or temporary storage of automobiles, travel trailers
and/or boats of the occupants of the premises, and wherein:
      (1)   Not more than one space is rented for parking to persons not
resident on the premises;
      (2)   Not more than two commercial vehicles per dwelling unit are parked
or stored; and
      (3)   The commercial vehicle permitted does not exceed two tons capacity.
   GARAGE, SERVICE STATION. Buildings and premises where gasoline, oil, grease,
batteries, tires and motor vehicle accessories may be supplied and dispensed at
retail. Uses permissible at a filling station do not include major mechanical
and body work, straightening of body parts, painting, welding, storage of
automobiles not in operational condition or other work involving noise, glare,
fumes, smoke or other characteristics to an extent greater than normally found
in filling stations. A filling station is not a repair garage nor a body shop.
   HOME OCCUPATION. An occupation conducted in a dwelling unit, provided that:
      (1)   The use of the dwelling unit for the home occupation shall be
clearly incidental and subordinate to its use for residential purposes by its
occupants and not more than 25% of the floor area of the dwelling unit shall be
used in the conduct of the home occupation;
      (2)   There shall be no change in the outside appearance of the building
or premises, or other visible evidence of the conduct of such home occupation,
other than one sign, not exceeding four square feet in area, non-illuminated
and mounted flat against the wall of the principal building; and
      (3)   No equipment or process shall be used in such home occupation which
creates noise, glare, vibration, fumes, odors or electrical interference
detectable to the normal senses off the lot, if the occupation is conducted in
a single-family residence, or outside the dwelling unit if conducted in other
than a single-family residence. In the case of electrical interference, no
equipment or process shall be used which creates visual or audible interference
in any radio or television receivers off the premises, or causes fluctuations
in line voltage off the premises.
   IMPROVEMENT LOCATION PERMIT. A permit signed by the Building Commissioner
stating that a proposed improvement complies with the provisions of this
chapter and such other laws as may be applicable.
   JUNK BUILDINGS, JUNK SHOPS or JUNK YARDS. Any land, property, structure,
building or combination of the same on which junk is stored or processed.
   LOADING SPACE, OFF STREET. Space logically and conveniently located for bulk
pickups and deliveries, scaled to delivery vehicles expected to be used, and
accessible to such vehicles expected to be used, and accessible to such
vehicles when required off-street parking spaces are filled; required off-
street parking space in computation of required off-street parking space. All
OFF-STREET LOADING SPACES shall be located totally outside of any street or
alley right-of way.
   MANUFACTURING EXTRACTIVE. Any mining, quarrying, excavating, processing,
storing, separating, cleaning or marketing of any mineral natural resource.
   MANUFACTURING, HEAVY. Manufacturing, processing, assembling, storing,
testing and similar industrial uses which are generally major operations and
extensive in character; require large sites, open storage and service areas,
extensive services and facilities and ready access to regional transportation;
and normally generate some nuisances such as smoke, noise, vibration, dust,
glare, air pollution and water pollution, but not beyond the district boundary.
   MANUFACTURING, LIGHT. Manufacturing or other industrial uses which are
usually controlled operations; relatively clean, quiet and free of
objectionable or hazardous elements such as smoke, noises, odor or dust;
operating and storing within enclosed structures; and generating little
industrial traffic and no nuisances.
   MOBILE HOME PARK. Any site, lot, field or tract of land under single
ownership, or ownership of two or more persons upon which two or more mobile
homes to be used for human habitation are parked, either free of charge or for
revenue purposes, and shall include any highway used or intended for use as
part of the facilities of such mobile home park. A MOBILE HOME PARK does not
include a mobile home sales area on which unoccupied mobile homes are parked
for inspection or sale.
   NOISE. Noise which is determined to be objectionable because of volume,
frequency or beat shall be muffled or otherwise controlled. Fire sirens and
related apparatus used solely for public purposes shall be exempt from this
requirement.
   NONCONFORMING USE. A building, structure or use of land existing at the time
of the enactment of this chapter and which does not conform to the regulations
of the district or zone in which it is situated.
   PLANNED UNIT DEVELOPMENT. An area of land in which a variety of housing
types or related commercial and industrial facilities are accommodated in a
pre-planned environment under more flexible standards, such as lot sizes and
setbacks, than those restrictions that would normally apply under these
regulations. The procedure for approval of such development contains
requirements in addition to those of the standard subdivision, such as building
design principles and landscaping plans.
   PUBLIC USES. Public parks, schools and administrative and cultural buildings
and structures, not including public land or buildings devoted solely to the
storage and maintenance of equipment and materials and public service
facilities.
   QUASI-PUBLIC USE. Churches, synagogues, temples, Sunday schools, parochial
schools, colleges, hospitals and other facilities of an educational, religious,
charitable, philanthropic or nonprofit nature.
   ROADSIDE STAND. A temporary structure designed or used for the display or
sale of agricultural and related products.
   SET BACK and LOT LINES. As described and shown in Appendix A of this
chapter.
   SIGN. Any device intended to inform or attract
the attention of persons not on the premises on which the sign is located.
   SUPPLY YARDS. A commercial establishment storing and offering for sale
building supplies, steel supplies, coal, heavy equipment, feed and grain and
similar goods.
   USE. The specific purposes for which land or a building is designated,
arranged or intended, or for which it is or may be occupied or maintained.
   VARIANCE. A modification of the strict terms of the relevant regulations
where such modification will not be contrary to the public interest and where
owing to conditions peculiar to the property and not the result of the action
of the applicant, a literal enforcement of this chapter would result in
unnecessary and undue hardship.
   VETERINARY ANIMAL HOSPITAL OR CLINIC. A place used for the care, grooming,
diagnosis and treatment of sick, ailing, infirm or injured animals, and those
who are in need of medical or surgical attention, and may include overnight
accommodations on the premises for the treatment, observation or recuperation.
   YARD. A required open space, other than a court, unoccupied and unobstructed
by any structure or portion of a structure from three feet above the general
ground level of the graded lot upward; provided, accessories, ornaments and
furniture may be permitted in any yard, subject to height limitations and
requirements limiting the obstruction of visibility.
   YARD, FRONT. A yard extending between side lot lines across the front of a
lot and from the front lot line to the front of the principal building.
   YARD, REAR. A yard extending between side lot lines across the rear of a lot
and from the rear lot line to the rear of the principal building.
   YARD, SIDE. A yard extending from the principal building to the side lot
line on both sides of the principal building between the lines establishing the
front and rear yards.
   ZONING BOARD. The Town Board of Zoning Appeals.
   ZONING PERMIT. A document authorizing the use of lots, structures, uses of
land and structures and the characteristics of the uses.
(Prior Code, § 152.001) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
ZONING MAP; DISTRICT BOUNDARIES
§ 154.015 ESTABLISHMENT AND PURPOSE OF DISTRICTS.
   (A)   Low Density Residential District (R-1). The purpose of the R-
1 District is to permit the establishment of low density single-family
residential uses, but not to exceed six dwelling units per gross acre. Town
water and sewer facilities shall be required.
   (B)   Medium-Low Density Residential District (R-2). The purpose of the R-
2 District is to encourage the establishment of medium-low density multi-family
residential uses, not to exceed 12 dwelling units per gross acre. Town water
and sewer facilities are required.
   (C)   Medium-High Density Multi-Family Residential District (R-3). The
purpose of the R-3 District is to encourage the establishment of medium- high
density multi-family residential uses, not to exceed 18 dwelling units per
gross acre. All such districts must abut upon either an arterial or collector
street and have town water and sewer facilities.
   (D)   Central Business District (CB). The purpose of the CB District is to
accommodate and encourage further expansion and renewal in the historical core
business area of the community. A variety of business, institutional, public,
quasi-public, cultural, residential and other related uses are encouraged in an
effort to provide the mix of activities necessary to establish a truly urban
character.
   (E)   General Business District (GB). The purpose of the GB District is to
encourage the establishment of areas for general business uses to meet the
needs of a regional market area. Activities in this district are often large
space users, and the customers using such facilities generally do not make
frequent purchases. Shopping centers will be the predominant building approach.
Strip development shall be prohibited. GB Districts shall be located on
arterial streets as specified in the Major Thoroughfare Plan.
   (F)   Light Industrial District (I-1). The purpose of the I-1 District is to
encourage the development of manufacturing and wholesale business
establishments which are clean, quiet and free of hazardous or objectionable
elements, such as noise, odor, dust, smoke or glare; operate entirely within
enclosed structures; and generate little industrial traffic. Research
activities are encouraged. This district is further designed to act as a
transitional use between heavy industrial uses and other less intense business
and residential uses.
   (G)   Heavy Industrial District (I-2). The purpose of the I-2 District is to
encourage the development of major manufacturing, processing, warehousing and
major research and testing operations. These activities require extensive
community facilities and reasonable access to arterial highways; they may have
extensive open storage and service areas and generate heavy traffic, but shall
be prohibited if they create nuisances beyond the limitations set up by the
Commission.
   (H)   Agricultural District (A). The purpose of the A District is to
preserve and protect the decreasing supply of prime agricultural land. This
district also is established to control the indiscriminate infiltration of
urban development in agricultural areas, which adversely affects agricultural
operators.
   (I)   Floodplain District (F.P.D.). The purpose of the Floodplain District
is to safeguard the area likely to be flooded once every 100 years as
designated by the Federal Insurance Administrator and having special flood
hazards as provided by the Flood Disaster Protection Act of 1973, being 42
U.S.C. §§ 4001 et seq.
(Prior Code, § 152.015) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
§ 154.016 OFFICIAL ZONING MAP.
   (A)   Adoption. The districts established in §
154.015 of this chapter are shown on the Official Zoning Map, which, together
with all explanatory matter thereon, is hereby adopted and incorporated into
this chapter as set out in Appendix B of this chapter.
   (B)   Identification. The Official Zoning Map shall be identified by the
signature of the Town Council members and attested by the Clerk/Treasurer, and
bearing the town seal.
(Prior Code, § 152.016) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
§ 154.017 INTERPRETATION OF DISTRICT BOUNDARIES.
   Where uncertainty exists concerning the zoning district shown on the
Official Zoning Map, the following rules shall apply.
   (A)   Where district boundaries are indicated as approximately following the
centerlines of streets or highways, street lines or highway right-of-way lines,
the centerlines, street lines or highway right-of-way lines shall be construed
to be the actual boundaries.
   (B)   Where district boundaries are indicated as approximately following the
lot lines, the lot lines shall be construed to be the actual boundaries.
   (C)   Where district boundaries are indicated as approximately parallel to
the centerlines or street lines of streets or the centerlines or right-of-way
lines of highways, the district boundaries shall be construed as being parallel
to them and at such distance therefrom as indicated on the Official Zoning Map.
If no distance is given, the dimensions shall be determined by the use of the
scale shown on the Official Zoning Map.
   (D)   Where the boundary of a district follows a railroad line, the boundary
shall be deemed to be located in the centerline of the main tracks of the
railroad line.
(Prior Code, § 152.017) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
§ 154.018 SCHEDULE OF DISTRICT REGULATIONS ADOPTED.
   The Schedule of District Regulations as set out in Appendix C of this
chapter is adopted and incorporated into this chapter. The requirements set
forth in that schedule shall govern uses in the districts.
(Prior Code, § 152.018) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
§ 154.019 FLOODPLAIN DISTRICT.
   (A)   Designation of flood hazard areas. The Floodplain District, as shown
on the Zoning Map, designates lands within the town which are likely to be
flooded once every 100 years and which have been designated by the Federal
Insurance Administrator as having special flood hazards as provided by 42
U.S.C. §§ 4001 et seq., as amended.
   (B)   Provisions and regulations.
      (1)   Any open uses of land, including agricultural and recreational
uses, shall be permitted in the Floodplain District.
      (2)   Any structure used for residential (excepting mobile homes),
business, industrial, public or quasi-public purposes, any structure incidental
to any agricultural or recreational use and any major repairs to an existing
structure may be permitted by the Zoning Board in the Floodplain District only
in accordance with the special permit procedure in division (C) below.
   (C)   Special permit procedure.
      (1)   Upon receipt of an application for a special permit by the property
owner, the Clerk/Treasurer shall set a date for a hearing, notify the applicant
and notify any person or governmental unit having a probable interest in the
proposal, including the State Natural Resources Commission.
      (2)   The Zoning Board may then, after a hearing according to law, grant
the special permit only after it has considered the recommendation of the State
Natural Resources Commission and only if conditions, restrictions and
requirements are imposed on the use to assure that the use, construction or
major repair:
         (a)   Uses construction materials and utility equipment that are
resistant to flood damage;
         (b)   Uses construction practices and methods that will minimize flood
damage;
         (c)   Is designed or modified and anchored to prevent flotation,
collapse or lateral movement of the structure; and
         (d)   Avoids impairment of, or contamination from, on-site waste
disposal systems during flooding.
   (D)   Variances. The Zoning Board may not grant a variance to any of the
requirements of the Floodplain District without the written approval of the
State Natural Resources Commission.
   (E)   Continuation of nonconforming uses. The lawful use of a building or
premises existing at the time of passage of the ordinance codified in this
chapter may be continued although such use does not conform to the provisions
of this chapter.
   (F)   Improvement of nonconforming uses. A nonconforming use in the
Floodplain District may be altered, enlarged or extended on a one-time basis if
the procedures set forth in this chapter are followed and if the alterations,
enlargements or extensions do not increase the value of the building or
structure, excluding the value of land, by more than 40% of its pre-improvement
market value, unless such building or structure is permanently changed to a
conforming use.
(Prior Code, § 152.019) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
MOBILE HOMES AND PARKS;
MANUFACTURED HOUSING
§ 154.030 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CLEAR DISTANCE. The unobstructed distance from any given point, mobile home
or line to the closest point or points of an adjacent mobile home or mobile
homes.
   MOBILE HOME. Any vehicle without motive power designated by the manufacturer
or maker, with hitch and undercarriage to permit the attachment of axles and
wheels, and so designed to permit its being used as a conveyance upon public
highways, and so designed, constructed or reconstructed as will permit the
vehicle to be used as a single-family dwelling.
   MOBILE HOME PARK. Any site or tract of land under single ownership upon
which one or more mobile homes used for habitation are parked, either free of
charge or for revenue purposes; including any roadway, building, structure,
vehicle or enclosure used or intended for use as a part of the facilities of
such park.
   MOBILE HOME PARK STREET. A public or private way other than an alley which
affords a primary means of access to abutting property within a mobile home
park.
   MOBILE HOME SUBDIVISION. Any site, lot, field or tract of land under single
ownership or the ownership of two or more persons which is to be divided into
smaller sites, lots, fields or tracts of land, which smaller sites, lots,
fields or tracts of land are to be sold for use by the purchaser to park the
purchaser’s mobile home.
   PRE-EXISTING MOBILE HOME. Any mobile home which has been placed upon a lot,
tract of ground or acreage within the town and is being used as a dwelling
place at the time of the passage of the ordinance codified in this subchapter.
   RECREATIONAL VEHICLE. A portable vehicular structure designed as a temporary
dwelling for travel and vacation uses which:
      (1)   Is identified on the unit by the manufacturer as a travel trailer,
is not more than eight feet in body width and is of any weight, provided its
body length does not exceed 29 feet; and
      (2)   Is a structure mounted on an automobile or truck and designed to be
used for sleeping and human habitation.
   RECREATIONAL VEHICLE PARK. Any site, lot, field or tract of land under
single ownership or the ownership of two or more people, designed with
facilities for short-term occupancy by recreational vehicles only.
(Prior Code, § 152.030) (Ord. 385, passed 6-14-1982)
§ 154.031 LOCATION REQUIREMENTS FOR MOBILE HOMES OR RECREATIONAL VEHICLES.
   (A)   No mobile home which is to be used or which can be used as a dwelling
place shall be permitted to be placed or located within the town, except within
a mobile home park. This does not apply to pre-existing mobile homes as defined
by §
154.030 of this chapter.
   (B)   No pre-existing mobile home shall be relocated within the town except
within a mobile home park.
   (C)   No real estate whereupon a pre-existing mobile home is situated shall
be used for the location of any other mobile home unless it qualifies as a
mobile home park as defined by §
154.030 of this chapter.
   (D)   No other mobile home shall be permitted upon a pre-existing mobile
home site unless the pre- existing mobile home is removed and, within ten days
thereafter, said pre-existing mobile home is replaced by a mobile home of
comparable or greater value and of similar or larger size and quality.
   (E)   No recreational vehicle shall be permitted to be used as a place for
sleeping and human habitation for a period in excess of 14 days within the
town, except within a recreational vehicle park.
(Prior Code, § 152.031) (Ord. 385, passed 6-14-1982) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.032 DESIGN REQUIREMENTS FOR MOBILE HOME PARKS.
   (A)   Each mobile home park shall contain a minimum of five acres.
   (B)   Mobile home stands must be so located that when occupied by a mobile
home, the clear distance between a mobile home and any adjacent mobile home
will be not less than 20 feet, except for end-to-end clear distance, which may
not be less than ten feet.
   (C)   No mobile home shall be located closer than 20 feet to any building
within the mobile home park.
   (D)   (1)   The minimum depth of the front yard of a mobile home park where
such park abuts a major arterial street shall be 60 feet.
      (2)   The minimum depth of the front yard of a mobile home park where
such park abuts a minor arterial street shall be 40 feet.
      (3)   The minimum depth of the front yard of a mobile home park where
such park abuts a local street shall be 25 feet.
   (E)   The minimum depth of side and rear yards of a mobile home park shall
be 25 feet, and when so provided, the minimum depth of side and rear yards
shall be ten feet.
   (F)   Each mobile home or mobile home stand or mobile home space shall be
provided with two parking spaces adjacent thereto, which parking spaces shall
have unobstructed access to a mobile home park street. On-street parking shall
be permitted where the street is not less than 32 feet wide.
   (G)   The clear distance between any mobile home and the centerline of the
abutting mobile home park street shall be a minimum of 25 feet.
   (H)   Each mobile home shall have access to, and the use of, general storage
space of a minimum of 90 cubic feet in a building of fire-proof design. Storage
space under the mobile home may be used if the storage is shielded from view by
underpinning the mobile home.
   (I)   Mobile home park streets shall be paved either with portland cement
concrete or bituminous concrete, including the surfacing procedure commonly
known as “chip and seal.” Such streets shall be a minimum of 24 feet in width
and shall, if publicly maintained, be built in conformance with the current
street construction standards of the town.
   (J)   Surface draining shall be installed and maintained by the owner or his
or her successor in title.
   (K)   There shall be a maximum of two entrances to a mobile home park.
   (L)   A maximum of nine mobile homes shall be permitted per acre. This
maximum shall be determined from the gross acreage of the mobile home park.
   (M)   Mobile home parks, where permitted, shall be in accordance with I.C.
13-17-1-1 et seq., as amended, and 410 I.A.C. 6-6-1 et seq., as amended.
(Prior Code, § 152.032) (Ord. 385, passed 6-14-1982) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.033 RECREATIONAL VEHICLE PARKS.
   The procedure for a recreational vehicle park shall be as provided herein
for a mobile home park, and the design, installation and maintenance shall be
as required by the State Board of Health.
(Prior Code, § 152.033) (Ord. 385, passed 6-14-1982) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.034 DESIGN REQUIREMENTS FOR MOBILE HOME SUBDIVISIONS.
   (A)   The minimum area of a mobile home subdivision shall be ten acres.
   (B)   The wheels shall be removed from each mobile home occupying a lot in
the subdivision.
   (C)   If a permanent solid foundation is not provided, all sides of the
mobile home shall be properly screened with skirts to shield the mobile home
undercarriage, and the mobile home shall be provided with a stand consisting of
either a solid concrete slab or two concrete ribbons of a thickness and size
adequate to support the maximum anticipated loads during all seasons. When
concrete ribbons are used, the area between the ribbons shall be filled with a
layer of crushed rock or asphalt. Each concrete stand shall be provided with an
anchor ring for each corner of the mobile home able to sustain a minimum
tensile strength of 2,800 pounds.
   (D)   Each mobile home occupying a lot in the subdivision shall contain a
flush toilet, sleeping accommodations, a tub or shower bath, kitchen facilities
and plumbing and electrical connections designed for and attached to
appropriate external systems.
   (E)   A dense belt of evergreen trees or shrubs not less than five feet high
after one full growing season, and which at maturity is not less than ten feet
high, shall be provided by the subdivider along all subdivision boundary lines
except at established street entrances and exits serving the subdivision.
   (F)   The minimum residential lot size in subdivisions served by a public
sewer system shall be 5,000 square feet, and the minimum lot width 50 feet.
   (G)   The minimum residential lot size indicated in division (F) above
served by septic tank systems shall be appropriately expanded in accordance
with adequate percolation tests certified by the performing engineer or land
surveyor, and related to proper absorption fields approved by the State Board
of Health.
   (H)   Each mobile home shall have a minimum ten feet of side yard on each
side. SIDE YARD means the area that extends between the outside wall of the
mobile home or accessory structure and the nearest side lot line.
   (I)   The minimum front yard setback for single- family dwellings of the
district in which the subdivision is located shall be adhered to by each mobile
home.
(Prior Code, § 152.034) (Ord. 385, passed 6-14-1982) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.035 ENFORCEMENT OF PROVISIONS; ABATEMENT AS A NUISANCE.
   (A)   Any person may, by suit in a court with jurisdiction, enjoin any
violation of §§
154.030 through
154.035 of this chapter.
   (B)   A use that violates the provisions of this subchapter shall be treated
as if it were a common nuisance, and it may be abated in the same manner as
such a nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 152.035) (Ord. 385, passed 6-14-1982)
§ 154.036 MANUFACTURED HOUSING.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      MANUFACTURED HOME. A dwelling unit, placed onto a permanent foundation,
which was fabricated on or after June 15, 1976, in an offsite manufacturing
facility for installation or assembly at the building site, bearing a seal
certifying that it is built in compliance with the Federal Manufacturing
Housing Construction and Safety Standards Code or I.C. 22-15-4 et seq., as
promulgated by the State Administrative Building Council.
      MANUFACTURED HOUSING CONSTRUCTION AND SAFETY STANDARDS CODE. Title IV of
the 1974 Housing and Community Development Act, 42 U.S.C. §§ 5401 et seq., as
amended (previously known as the federal Mobile Home Construction and Safety
Act), rules and regulations adopted thereunder, which include the Department of
Housing and Urban Development- approved information supplied by the home
manufacturer, and regulations and interpretations of the code by the State
Administrative Building Council.
      ONE- AND TWO-FAMILY DWELLING CODE. The mandatory statewide building code
adopted by the State Administrative Building Council for one- and two-family
residential dwellings.
      SPECIAL EXCEPTION PERMIT. A device for permitting a use within a district
other than a principally permitted one.
   (B)   Permitted placement. The establishment, location and use of
manufactured homes as scattered- site residences shall be permitted in any zone
permitting installation of a dwelling unit subject to requirements and
limitations applying generally to such residential use in the district, and
provided such homes shall meet the following requirements and limitations.
      (1)   The home shall meet all requirements applicable to single-family
dwellings and possess all necessary improvements, building and occupancy
permits and other certification required by the code.
      (2)   The home shall be of double-sections construction and meet the
minimum square footage requirements for the appropriate zone.
      (3)   The home shall be attached and anchored to a permanent foundation
in conformance with the regulations in the State One- and Two-Family Dwelling
Code and with the manufacturer’s installation specifications.
      (4)   The home shall be covered with an exterior material customarily
used on site-built residential dwellings, and such material shall extend over
the top of the foundation or comply with the town site-built residential
dwelling home standards.
      (5)   The home shall have a roof composed of a material customarily used
on site-built residential dwellings, such as asbestos, fiberglass, shake,
asphalt or tile, which shall be installed onto a surface appropriately pitched
for the materials used.
   (C)   Standards for manufactured housing. The Board establishes the
following standards for manufactured housing.
      (1)   Manufactured homes shall be at least 23 feet in width and 950
square feet of occupied space.
      (2)   The main body of the house shall be a rectangle.
      (3)   The main roof shall be pitched rather than flat.
      (4)   The house shall face the street, and ordinarily shall be parallel
to the street.
      (5)   The exterior walls shall resemble wood or masonry regardless of the
actual composition.
      (6)   The main roof shall be shingled.
      (7)   The foundations shall form a complete enclosure under exterior
walls.
      (8)   Apparent bulk shall be about the same throughout the neighborhood.
An occasional larger house may be allowed, but none shall be permitted that
look substantially smaller than the general run.
   (D)   Placement with permit. The persons placing homes in these districts
shall obtain a special exception permit from the Zoning Board:
      (1)   Residential Zone 1 (R-1);
      (2)   Residential Zone 2 (R-2); and
      (3)   Residential Zone 3 (R-3).
   (E)   Violations; abatement.
      (1)   A home sited upon property in violation of this section shall be
subject to removal from such property. However, the homeowner shall be given a
reasonable opportunity to bring the property into compliance before action for
removal can be taken. If action is taken by the appropriate authority to ensure
compliance with this section, the expenses involved shall be made a lien
against the property.
      (2)   The Commission or its designated administrator may institute a suit
in an appropriate court for injunctive relief to cause such violation to be
prevented, abated or removed.
(Prior Code, § 152.036) (Ord. 385, passed 6-14-1982) Penalty, see §
154.999
Statutory reference:
   Manufactured housing, see I.C. 36-7-4-1106
SUPPLEMENTARY DISTRICT REGULATIONS
§ 154.050 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of supplementary district regulations is to establish conditions
for various uses, classifications of uses or areas where problems are
frequently encountered.
(Prior Code, § 152.050) (Ord. 357, passed - -1973)
§ 154.051 PRIVATE SWIMMING POOLS.
   No private swimming pool, exclusive of portable swimming pools with a
diameter of less than 12 feet or with an area of less than 100 square feet,
shall be allowed in any commercial or residential district, except as an
accessory use and unless it complies with the following conditions and
requirements.
   (A)   The pool is intended and is to be used solely for the enjoyment of the
occupants of the principal use of the property on which it is located.
   (B)   The pool is not located closer than ten feet to any property line.
   (C)   The pool, or the entire property on which it is located, is walled or
fenced to prevent uncontrolled access by children and animals from the street
or from adjacent properties. The fence or wall shall not be less than six feet
in height, shall be maintained in good condition with a gate and lock and shall
be erected within 30 days of the date the pool is installed.
(Prior Code, § 152.051) (Ord. 357, passed - -1973) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.052 TEMPORARY BUILDINGS.
   Temporary buildings, construction trailers and equipment and materials used
in conjunction with construction work only may be permitted in any district
during the period construction work is in progress, but such temporary
facilities shall be removed upon completion of the construction work. Storage
of such facilities or equipment beyond the completion date of the project shall
require a zoning permit authorized by the Zoning Board.
(Prior Code, § 152.052) (Ord. 357, passed - -1973) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.053 PARKING AND STORAGE OF CERTAIN VEHICLES.
   Automotive vehicles or trailers of any kind or type without current license
plates shall not be parked or stored on any residentially-zoned property other
than in completely enclosed buildings. One boat and one trailer may be stored
in the rear yard if they have a current license.
(Prior Code, § 152.053) (Ord. 357, passed - -1973) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.054 SETBACK REQUIREMENTS FOR CORNER BUILDINGS.
   On a corner lot, the principal building and its accessory structures shall
be required to have the same setback distance from all street right-of-way
lines as required for the front yard in the district in which such structures
are located.
(Prior Code, § 152.054) (Ord. 357, passed - -1973) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.055 VISIBILITY AT INTERSECTIONS IN RESIDENTIAL DISTRICTS.
   Nothing shall be erected, placed, planted or allowed to grow on a corner lot
in any residential district which materially impedes vision above a height of
two and one-half feet over the centerline grades of the intersecting streets.
(Prior Code, § 152.055) (Ord. 357, passed - -1973) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.056 FENCE AND WALL RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   No fence or wall shall be erected without a permit.
   (B)   No fence or wall surrounding the entire yard and greater than six feet
in height shall be erected. No decorative fence, wall or vegetation used as
fencing shall be permitted in any required front yard if it is greater than 30
inches in height.
   (C)   All fences, walls and vegetation used as fencing shall be maintained.
(Prior Code, § 152.056) (Ord. 357, passed - -1973) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.057 EXCEPTIONS TO HEIGHT REGULATIONS.
   The height limitations contained in this chapter do not apply to spires,
belfries, cupolas, antennas, water tanks, ventilators, chimneys or other
appurtenances usually required to be placed above the roof level and not
intended for human occupancy, except where the height of such structures
constitutes a hazard to the safe landing and takeoff of aircraft at an
established airport.
(Prior Code, § 152.057) (Ord. 357, passed - -1973) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.058 NOISE; VIBRATION.
   (A)   Noise. Noise deemed objectionable by the Zoning Board due to volume,
frequency or beat shall be muffled or otherwise controlled. Objectionable noise
related solely to public purposes are exempt from this division (A).
   (B)   Vibration. No vibration shall be permitted which is discernable
without instruments on any adjoining lot or property.
(Prior Code, § 152.058) (Ord. 357, passed - -1973) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.059 AIR POLLUTION.
   No pollution of air by fly-ash dust, vapors, odors, smoke or other
substances shall be permitted which is harmful to health, animals, vegetation
or other property, or which can cause excessive soiling.
(Prior Code, § 152.059) (Ord. 357, passed - -1973) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.060 PLANS FOR REDUCING DANGEROUS OR OBJECTIONABLE ELEMENTS; MEASUREMENT
PROCEDURE.
   (A)   Plans for reducing dangerous or objectionable elements. The Zoning
Inspector or the Zoning Board, prior to the issuance of a zoning permit, may
require the submission of statements and plans indicating the manner in which
dangerous and objectionable elements involved in processing and in equipment
operations are to be eliminated or reduced to acceptable limits and tolerances.
   (B)   Measurement procedures. Methods and procedures for the determination
of the existence of any dangerous and objectionable elements shall conform to
the latest edition of the applicable standard measurement procedures published
by the American Standards Association, Inc., New York; the Manufacturing
Chemists’ Association, Inc., Washington, D.C.; the United States Bureau of
Mines and the State Water and Air Pollution Control Board.
(Prior Code, § 152.060) (Ord. 357, passed - -1973) Penalty, see §
154.999
OFF-STREET PARKING AND LOADING
REQUIREMENTS
§ 154.075 LOCATION OF PARKING SPACES.
   The following regulations shall govern the location of off-street parking
spaces and areas: parking spaces for all detached residential uses shall be
located on the same lot as the use which they are intended to serve.
(Prior Code, § 152.070) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.076 SCREENING OR LANDSCAPING.
   Whenever a parking area is located in or adjacent to a residential district,
it shall be effectively screened on all sides which adjoin or face any property
used for residential purposes by an acceptably designed wall, fence or planting
screen not less than four feet nor more than six feet in height, maintained in
good condition. The space between such fence, wall or planting screen and the
lot line of the adjoining premises in any residential district shall be
landscaped with grass, hardy shrubs or evergreen ground cover and maintained in
good condition. If the terrain or other natural features preclude the erection
of such fence, wall or planting screen from serving the intended purpose, then
no such fence, wall or planting screen and landscaping shall be required at the
discretion of the Zoning Board.
(Prior Code, § 152.071) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.077 WHEEL BLOCKS.
   Whenever a parking lot extends to a property line, wheel blocks or other
suitable devices shall be installed to prevent any part of a parked vehicle
from extending beyond the property line.
(Prior Code, § 152.072) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.078 WIDTH OF DRIVEWAYS.
   Driveways serving individual parking spaces shall not be less than 25 feet
wide for 90-degree parking, 12 feet wide for parallel parking, 17.5 feet for
60-degree parking and 13 feet for 45-degree parking.
(Prior Code, § 152.073) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.079 ACCESS TO PARKING AREAS.
   Any parking area shall be designed so that any vehicle leaving or entering
the parking area from or into a public or private street shall be traveling in
a forward motion. Driveways for parking areas or loading spaces shall be
designed so that any vehicle entering or leaving the lot shall be clearly
visible for a reasonable distance to any pedestrian or motorist approaching the
access or driveway from a public or private street.
(Prior Code, § 152.074) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.080 STRIPING.
   All parking areas with a capacity for over 12 vehicles shall be striped.
(Prior Code, § 152.075) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.081 PARKING SPACE REQUIREMENTS.
   For the purposes of this chapter, the following parking space requirements
shall apply:
   (A)   Residential.
      (1)   Single-family or two-family dwelling: two for each unit; and
      (2)   Multi-family dwelling: two for each unit.
   (B)   Commercial. All types of business or commercial uses permitted in any
commercial district: one for each 300-square foot area, plus one for each
employee; and
   (C)   Industrial. All types of manufacturing, storage and wholesale uses
permitted in any industrial district: one for every employee on the largest
shift for which the building is designed, plus one for each motor vehicle used
in the business.
(Prior Code, § 152.076) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
SIGNS
§ 154.095 INTENT AND PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this subchapter is to promote and protect the public health,
welfare and safety by regulating existing and proposed outdoor advertising,
outdoor advertising signs, posters and outdoor signs of all types.
   (A)   It is intended to protect property values, create a more attractive
economic and business climate, enhance and protect the physical appearance of
the community and preserve the scenic and natural beauty of designated areas.
   (B)   It is intended to reduce sign or advertising distractions and
obstructions which may contribute to traffic accidents, reduce hazards which
may be caused by signs overhanging or projecting over public rights-of-way,
provide more open space and curb the deterioration of the natural environment
and enhance community development.
(Prior Code, § 152.090) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
§ 154.096 MEASUREMENT OF SIGN AREA.
   The surface area of a sign shall be computed to include the entire area
within a regular, geometric form, or a combination of regular geometric forms,
comprising all of the display area of the sign and including all of the
elements of the matter displayed. Frames and structural members not being
advertising matter shall not be included in the computation of the surface
area.
(Prior Code, § 152.091) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
§ 154.097 SIGNS PERMITTED UNDER CERTAIN CONDITIONS.
   (A)   Signs permitted in all districts without a permit. The following signs
shall be permitted in all districts without a permit:
      (1)   Signs advertising the sale, lease or rental of the premises upon
which the sign is located, not exceeding 12 feet in area, except in residential
districts, where the area of the sign shall not exceed six square feet;
      (2)   Professional name plates not exceeding four square feet in area;
      (3)   Signs denoting the name and address of the occupants of the
premises, not exceeding two square feet in area; and
      (4)   Political signs of any nature.
   (B)   Signs permitted in any district requiring a permit from the Planning
Commission. The following signs shall be permitted in any district following
the issuance of a permit by the Commission: signs or bulletin boards
customarily incidental to places of worship, libraries, museums, social clubs
or societies. The signs or bulletin boards shall not exceed 15 square feet in
area and shall be located on the premises of the institution.
   (C)   Signs permitted in commercial and industrial districts requiring a
permit.
      (1)   The regulations set forth in this division (C) shall apply to signs
in all commercial and industrial districts which require a permit.
      (2)   In a commercial or industrial district, each business shall be
permitted one flat or wall sign. Wall signs shall not project more than two
feet, as measured from the face of the main building. The area of all permanent
advertising signs for any single business enterprise may equal one and one-half
square feet of sign area for each lineal foot of building width, or part of a
building, occupied by the enterprise, but shall not exceed a maximum area of
100 square feet.
(Prior Code, § 152.092) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.098 FREESTANDING SIGNS.
   Freestanding signs not over 30 feet in height having a maximum total sign
area of 100 square feet per display area, and located not closer than ten feet
to any street right-of-way line and not closer than 30 feet to any adjoining
lot line, may be erected to serve a group of business establishments. There
shall be only one freestanding sign for each building, regardless of the number
of businesses conducted in the building.
(Prior Code, § 152.093) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.099 POLE SIGNS.
   (A)   Pole signs of symbolic design shall be permitted for business
establishments if no part of the sign projects into the right-of-way of any
street or highway. The maximum area of any face of the sign shall not exceed 30
square feet, and the pole support or the sign shall not be less than 50 feet
from any lot in any residential district.
   (B)   The location and design of any sign over 50 square feet must be
approved by the Commission before a permit shall be granted.
(Prior Code, § 152.094) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.100 WALL SIGNS PERTAINING TO NONCONFORMING USES.
   Wall signs pertaining to a nonconforming use shall be permitted on the same
premises of such use if the area of such sign does not exceed 12 square feet.
(Prior Code, § 152.095) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.101 SIGNS IN YARDS; REQUIREMENTS.
   Signs and advertising structures, where permitted, shall be erected or
placed in conformity with the side and rear yard requirements of the district
in which they are located, except that no sign or advertising structure shall
be erected or placed closer than 50 feet of a side or rear lot line in any
residential district.
(Prior Code, § 152.096) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.102 SIGNS OR POSTERS DESTRUCTIVE TO PUBLIC PROPERTY PROHIBITED.
   No sign or poster shall be posted in any place or in any manner that is
destructive to public property upon posting or removal.
(Prior Code, § 152.097) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
§ 154.115 ADMINISTRATIVE BODIES; RESPONSIBILITIES.
   (A)   Zoning Inspector; duties. For the purpose of this chapter, the Zoning
Inspector shall have the following duties:
      (1)   Upon finding that any of the provisions of this chapter are being
violated, the Inspector shall notify in writing the person responsible for such
violation(s), ordering the action necessary to correct such violation(s);
      (2)   Order the discontinuance of illegal uses of land, buildings or
structures;
      (3)   Order the removal of illegal buildings or structures or illegal
additions or structural alterations;
      (4)   Order the discontinuance of any illegal work being done;
      (5)   Take any other action authorized by this chapter to ensure
compliance with or to prevent violation(s) of this chapter. This may include
the issuance of and action on zoning permits and certificate of occupancy
permits and such similar administrative duties as are permissible under the
law; and
      (6)   The Zoning Inspector may be a member of the Plan Commission, chosen
by the Commission, subject to the approval of the Town Council, or another
officer chosen or hired by the Council. In the absence of a Zoning Inspector,
duties of the Zoning Inspector may be performed by the Town Building
Commissioner.
   (B)   Plan Commission.
      (1)   An advisory Town Plan Commission (Commission) is established under
I.C. 36-7-4 et seq. for all purposes set forth in that statute and other
provisions of state law, including without limitation, oversight of all
planning and zoning matters that affect the town, creating and amending
comprehensive land use plans, recommending changes to the zoning ordinances and
zoning map, recommending the approval or denial of proposals to subdivide or
rezone
land, adopt development plans or grant zoning variances, hold public meetings
and public hearings and receive comments from the public on all plans,
rezonings, variances or other changes to zoning or land use, inform the public
about the purpose of planning and how local problems are being addressed, and
name and number streets and structures.
      (2)   The Commission shall consist of seven members, at least four of
whom shall be citizen members appointed by the Town Council and the remainder
persons in town government appointed by the Council. Not more than two of the
citizen members shall be of the same political party. In appointing members,
whether citizen or ex officio, the Council shall take care to avoid actual or
potential conflicts of interest as defined in I.C. 36-7-4-223 and no members of
the Commission shall be related to each other in the first degree by birth or
marriage.
      (3)   Citizen members shall hold no other town office and shall meet the
qualifications of I.C. 36-7-4-207 and 36-7-4-216 and shall be chosen regarding
the criteria of I.C. 36-7-4-216. At least three citizen members shall be
qualified by reason of being residents of the jurisdiction area of the Plan
Commission.
      (4)   The citizen members of the Commission shall be appointed for a term
of four years or such staggered terms, not exceeding four years, as the Council
may provide.
      (5)   The Commission shall have the powers and duties set forth in I.C.
36-7-4 et seq. and other provisions of state law.
      (6)    The Commission shall meet as regularly as necessary and
appropriate considering the matters and tasks before it. The Commission shall
otherwise establish its own schedule and procedures, including rules for voting
and the conduct of meetings and hearings, within the parameters set by I.C. 36-
7-4-300 et seq. In the absence of such procedures, the Commission shall follow
“Robert’s Rules of Order”. All proceedings, including discussions, votes,
public comment and testimony and other evidence presented at hearings, of the
Commission shall comply with the Indiana Open Door Law and minutes and other
records of these proceedings shall be kept such detail and format as to be
readily reviewed by the Council and the public.
(Prior Code, § 152.110) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975; Ord. 2025-1, passed 1-8-
2025)
§ 154.116 ENFORCEMENT AGENT.
   The provisions of this chapter shall be enforced by the Town Building
Commissioner. No zoning permit or certificate of occupancy shall be granted by
him or her for any purpose except in compliance with the provisions of this
chapter.
(Prior Code, § 152.111) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
§ 154.117 PERMIT REQUIRED.
   No building or structure shall be erected, added to, or structurally altered
until a permit has been issued by the Building Commissioner, except upon a
written order of the Building Commissioner. No zoning permit or certificate of
occupancy shall be issued for any building where its construction, addition or
alteration, or use thereof, would be in violation of any of the provisions of
this chapter, except upon a written order of the Zoning Board.
(Prior Code, § 152.112) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975) Penalty, see §
154.999
§ 154.118 CERTIFICATE OF OCCUPANCY REQUIRED; RECORD TO BE KEPT.
   (A)   (1)   No land shall be occupied or used, and no building hereafter
erected, altered or extended shall be used or changed in use, until a
certificate of occupancy shall have been issued by the Building Commissioner
stating that the building or proposed use complies with the provisions of this
chapter.
      (2)   No nonconforming use shall be renewed, changed or extended until a
certificate of occupancy has been issued by the Building Commissioner.
      (3)   All certificates of occupancy shall be applied for at the same time
that the zoning permit is applied for.
   (B)   The Building Commissioner shall maintain a record of all certificates.
Copies shall be furnished, upon request, to any person having a proprietary or
tenancy interest in the building affected.
(Prior Code, § 152.113) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
§ 154.119 FILING FEES.
   Applications and petitions filed pursuant to the provisions of this chapter
shall be accompanied by the following filing fees. The fees shall be paid to
the Building Commissioner, who shall forward them promptly to the Clerk/
Treasurer, who shall deposit them in the Town General Fund.
   (A)   For each application for alterations, moving, repairs or additions to
all buildings or structures, the fee for the improvement location permit shall
be $2 for each $1,000, or fraction thereof, of the value of such alterations.
The value of the building or structure shall be based upon the amount of its
assessed valuation times three.
   (B)   For business or industrial buildings or structures, the fee for each
application for an improvement location permit shall be $3.50 for each $1,000,
or fraction thereof, of the value of such improvements, alterations, repairs or
additions.
   (C)   Accessory uses such as public utility installations, walks, driveways,
curbs, retaining walls, mail boxes, name plates, lamp posts, bird baths and
structures of a like nature do not require an improvement location permit.
   (D)   A fee of $1 shall be paid for each application for a certificate of
occupancy.
   (E)   A fee of $20 shall be paid for each petition for an appeal from any
decision of the Building Commissioner to the Zoning Board.
   (F)   A fee of $25 shall be paid for each petition for an amendment to this
chapter. Each petitioner shall pay for the required legal publications.
(Prior Code, § 152.114) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
§ 154.120 PERMIT EXPIRATION.
   The work or use authorized by any improvement location permit, or permit for
a variance, contingent use or other permit, except for an improvement location
permit for a special exception, must be commenced within six months of the date
of issuance of such permit or the permit shall lapse and be and become null and
void. All authorized work shall be completed within two years from the issuance
of the permit, except for a permit for a special exception. The Building
Commissioner may extend the work completion time upon a showing of good cause.
(Prior Code, § 152.115) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
§ 154.121 APPEAL PROCEDURE.
   Any person aggrieved or affected by any provision of this chapter or by any
decision of the Building Commissioner may appeal to the Zoning Board within a
reasonable time, as provided by the rules of the Board, by filing a notice of
appeal specifying the grounds for appeal. Every decision of the Zoning Board
shall be subject to review by certiorari.
(Prior Code, § 152.116) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
§ 154.122 VIOLATION DECLARED NUISANCE; REMEDIES.
   No person shall locate, erect, construct, reconstruct, enlarge, change,
maintain or use any structure or land in violation of any provision of this
chapter or of any regulation enacted by the Zoning Board. The Zoning Board or
the Commission may institute a suit for a mandatory injunction directing the
removal of a structure erected in violation of this chapter. Any structure or
use that violates this chapter shall be deemed to be a common nuisance, and the
owner of the structure or land shall be liable for maintaining a common
nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 152.117) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975)
§ 154.999 PENALTY.
   Any person who violates any provision of this chapter shall be fined not
less than $10 nor more than $300. Each day a violation continues constitutes a
separate offense.
(Prior Code, § 152.999) (Ord. 362, passed 4-8-1975; Ord. 385, passed 6-14-1982)
